<img alt="" class="noviewer" data-file-height="185" data-file-width="180" decoding="async" height="16" title="Category:Antisemitism">Category</a></td></tr><tr><td class="sidebar-navbar"><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1063604349">.mw-parser-output .navbar{display:inline;font-size:88%;font-weight:normal}.mw-parser-output .navbar-collapse{float:left;text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .navbar-boxtext{word-spacing:0}.mw-parser-output .navbar ul{display:inline-block;white-space:nowrap;line-height:inherit}.mw-parser-output .navbar-brackets::before{margin-right:-0.125em;content:"[ "}.mw-parser-output .navbar-brackets::after{margin-left:-0.125em;content:" ]"}.mw-parser-output .navbar li{word-spacing:-0.125em}.mw-parser-output .navbar a>span,.mw-parser-output .navbar a>abbr{text-decoration:inherit}.mw-parser-output .navbar-mini abbr{font-variant:small-caps;border-bottom:none;text-decoration:none;cursor:inherit}.mw-parser-output .navbar-ct-full{font-size:114%;margin:0 7em}.mw-parser-output .navbar-ct-mini{font-size:114%;margin:0 4em}</style><div class="navbar plainlinks hlist navbar-mini"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Antisemitism_sidebar" title="Template:Antisemitism sidebar"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Antisemitism_sidebar" title="Template talk:Antisemitism sidebar"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Antisemitism_sidebar&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Adolf Hitler</b> (<small>German: </small><span class="IPA" lang="de-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Standard_German" title="Help:IPA/Standard German">[ˈadoːlf ˈhɪt.lɐ]</a></span> <span class="nowrap" style="font-size:85%">(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:GT_AH_AMS.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" decoding="async" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/></a></span><a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/c/c9/GT_AH_AMS.ogg" title="GT AH AMS.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</span>; 20 April 1889 – 30 April 1945) was an Austrian-born German politician who was dictator of <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">Germany</a> from 1933 until <a href="/wiki/Death_of_Adolf_Hitler" title="Death of Adolf Hitler">his death</a> in 1945. <a href="/wiki/Adolf_Hitler%27s_rise_to_power" title="Adolf Hitler's rise to power">He rose to power</a> as the leader of the <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Party" title="Nazi Party">Nazi Party</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[a]</a></sup> becoming the <a href="/wiki/Chancellor_of_Germany" title="Chancellor of Germany">chancellor</a> in 1933 and then assuming the title of <span title="German-language text"><i lang="de"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/F%C3%BChrer_und_Reichskanzler" title="Führer und Reichskanzler">Führer und Reichskanzler</a></i></span> in 1934.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[b]</a></sup> During his <a href="/wiki/Dictatorship" title="Dictatorship">dictatorship</a>, he initiated <a href="/wiki/European_theatre_of_World_War_II" title="European theatre of World War II">World War II in Europe</a> by <a href="/wiki/Invasion_of_Poland" title="Invasion of Poland">invading Poland</a> on 1 September 1939. He was closely involved in military operations throughout the war and was central to the perpetration of <a href="/wiki/The_Holocaust" title="The Holocaust">the Holocaust</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Genocide" title="Genocide">genocide</a> of <a href="/wiki/Holocaust_victims" title="Holocaust victims">about six million Jews and millions of other victims</a>.
</p><p>Hitler was born in <a href="/wiki/Austria-Hungary" title="Austria-Hungary">Austria-Hungary</a> and was raised near <a href="/wiki/Linz" title="Linz">Linz</a>. He lived in Vienna later in the first decade of the 1900s and moved to Germany in 1913. He was decorated during his <a href="/wiki/Military_career_of_Adolf_Hitler" title="Military career of Adolf Hitler">service in the German Army</a> in <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>. In 1919, he joined the <a href="/wiki/German_Workers%27_Party" title="German Workers' Party">German Workers' Party</a> (DAP), the precursor of the Nazi Party, and was appointed leader of the Nazi Party in 1921. In 1923, he attempted to seize governmental power in <a href="/wiki/Beer_Hall_Putsch" title="Beer Hall Putsch">a failed coup in Munich</a> and was imprisoned with a sentence of five years. In jail, he dictated the first volume of his autobiography and political manifesto <span title="German-language text"><i lang="de"><a href="/wiki/Mein_Kampf" title="Mein Kampf">Mein Kampf</a></i></span> ("My Struggle"). After his early release in 1924, Hitler gained popular support by attacking the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Versailles" title="Treaty of Versailles">Treaty of Versailles</a> and promoting <a href="/wiki/Pan-Germanism" title="Pan-Germanism">pan-Germanism</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anti-Semitism" title="Anti-Semitism">anti-Semitism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Anti-communism" title="Anti-communism">anti-communism</a> with <a href="/wiki/Charismatic_authority" title="Charismatic authority">charismatic</a> oratory and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nazi_propaganda" title="Nazi propaganda">Nazi propaganda</a>. He frequently denounced international <a href="/wiki/Capitalism" title="Capitalism">capitalism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Communism" title="Communism">communism</a> as part of a <a href="/wiki/Antisemitic_canard" title="Antisemitic canard">Jewish conspiracy</a>.
</p><p>By November 1932, the Nazi Party held the most seats in the German <a href="/wiki/Reichstag_(Weimar_Republic)" title="Reichstag (Weimar Republic)">Reichstag</a>, but did not have a majority. As a result, no party was able to form a majority parliamentary coalition in support of a candidate for chancellor. The former chancellor <a href="/wiki/Franz_von_Papen" title="Franz von Papen">Franz von Papen</a> and other conservative leaders persuaded President <a href="/wiki/Paul_von_Hindenburg" title="Paul von Hindenburg">Paul von Hindenburg</a> to appoint Hitler as chancellor on 30 January 1933. Shortly after, the Reichstag passed the <a href="/wiki/Enabling_Act_of_1933" title="Enabling Act of 1933">Enabling Act of 1933</a> which began the process of transforming the <a href="/wiki/Weimar_Republic" title="Weimar Republic">Weimar Republic</a> into Nazi Germany, a <a href="/wiki/One-party_state" title="One-party state">one-party</a> dictatorship based on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Totalitarian" title="Totalitarian">totalitarian</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Autocratic" title="Autocratic">autocratic</a> ideology of <a href="/wiki/Nazism" title="Nazism">Nazism</a>. On 2 August 1934, Hindenburg died and Hitler replaced him as the head of state and government. Hitler aimed to eliminate Jews from Germany and establish a <a href="/wiki/New_Order_(Nazism)" title="New Order (Nazism)">New Order</a> to counter what he saw as the injustice of the post-World War I international order dominated by <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">Britain</a> and <a href="/wiki/French_Third_Republic" title="French Third Republic">France</a>. His first six years in power resulted in rapid economic recovery from the <a href="/wiki/Great_Depression" title="Great Depression">Great Depression</a>, the abrogation of restrictions imposed on Germany after World War I, and the annexation of territories inhabited by millions of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ethnic_Germans" title="Ethnic Germans">ethnic Germans</a>, which initially gave him significant popular support. 
</p><p>Hitler sought <span title="German-language text"><i lang="de"><a href="/wiki/Lebensraum" title="Lebensraum">Lebensraum</a></i></span> (<abbr title="literal translation">lit.</abbr><span style="white-space: nowrap;"> </span>'living space') for the German people in Eastern Europe, and his aggressive foreign policy is considered the primary <a href="/wiki/Causes_of_World_War_II" title="Causes of World War II">cause of World War II in Europe</a>. He directed large-scale rearmament and, on 1 September 1939, invaded Poland, resulting in Britain and France <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/British_and_French_declaration_of_war_on_Germany" title="British and French declaration of war on Germany">declaring war on Germany</a>. In June 1941, Hitler ordered an <a href="/wiki/Operation_Barbarossa" title="Operation Barbarossa">invasion of the Soviet Union</a>. By the end of 1941, German forces and the European <a href="/wiki/Axis_powers" title="Axis powers">Axis powers</a> occupied most of Europe and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/North_African_Campaign" title="North African Campaign">North Africa</a>. These gains were gradually reversed after 1941, and in 1945 the <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_II" title="Allies of World War II">Allied armies</a> defeated the German army. On 29 April 1945, he married his longtime lover, <a href="/wiki/Eva_Braun" title="Eva Braun">Eva Braun</a>, in the <span title="German-language text"><i lang="de"><a href="/wiki/F%C3%BChrerbunker" title="Führerbunker">Führerbunker</a></i></span> in Berlin. Less than two days later, the couple <a href="/wiki/Death_of_Adolf_Hitler" title="Death of Adolf Hitler">committed suicide</a> to avoid capture by the Soviet <a href="/wiki/Red_Army" title="Red Army">Red Army</a>. Their corpses were burned.
</p><p>The historian and biographer <a href="/wiki/Ian_Kershaw" title="Ian Kershaw">Ian Kershaw</a> describes Hitler as "the embodiment of modern political evil".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKershaw2000bxvii_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKershaw2000bxvii-6">[4]</a></sup> Under Hitler's leadership and <a href="/wiki/Nazi_racial_theories" title="Nazi racial theories">racially motivated ideology</a>, the Nazi regime was responsible for the genocide of about six million Jews and millions of other victims, whom he and his followers deemed <i><a href="/wiki/Untermensch" title="Untermensch">Untermenschen</a></i> (subhumans) or socially undesirable. Hitler and the Nazi regime were also responsible for the killing of an estimated 19.3 million civilians and prisoners of war. In addition, 28.7 million soldiers and civilians died as a result of military action in the European <a href="/wiki/Theater_(warfare)" title="Theater (warfare)">theatre</a>. The number of <a href="/wiki/World_War_II_casualties" title="World War II casualties">civilians killed</a> during World War II was unprecedented in warfare, and the casualties constitute the <a href="/wiki/List_of_wars_by_death_toll" title="List of wars by death toll">deadliest conflict in history</a>.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Ancestry">Ancestry</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Hitler_family" title="Hitler family">Hitler family</a></div>
<p>Hitler's father, <a href="/wiki/Alois_Hitler" title="Alois Hitler">Alois Hitler</a> (1837–1903), was the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Illegitimate" title="Illegitimate">illegitimate</a> child of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Maria_Anna_Schicklgruber" title="Maria Anna Schicklgruber">Maria Anna Schicklgruber</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBullock199924_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBullock199924-7">[5]</a></sup> The baptismal register did not show the name of his father, and Alois initially bore his mother's surname, <span title="German-language text"><span lang="de" style="font-style: normal;">'Schicklgruber'</span></span>. In 1842, <a href="/wiki/Johann_Georg_Hiedler" title="Johann Georg Hiedler">Johann Georg Hiedler</a> married Alois's mother. Alois was brought up in the family of Hiedler's brother, <a href="/wiki/Johann_Nepomuk_Hiedler" title="Johann Nepomuk Hiedler">Johann Nepomuk Hiedler</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMaser19734_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMaser19734-8">[6]</a></sup> In 1876, Alois was made legitimate and his baptismal record annotated by a priest to register Johann Georg Hiedler as Alois's father (recorded as "Georg Hitler").<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMaser197315_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMaser197315-9">[7]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKershaw19995_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKershaw19995-10">[8]</a></sup> Alois then assumed the surname "Hitler",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKershaw19995_10-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKershaw19995-10">[8]</a></sup> also spelled <span title="German-language text"><span lang="de" style="font-style: normal;">'Hiedler', 'Hüttler'</span></span>, or <span title="German-language text"><span lang="de" style="font-style: normal;">'Huettler'</span></span>. The name is probably based on the German word <span title="German-language text"><i lang="de">hütte</i></span> (lit., "hut"), and likely has the meaning "one who lives in a hut".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJetzinger197632_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJetzinger197632-11">[9]</a></sup>
</p><p>Nazi official <a href="/wiki/Hans_Frank" title="Hans Frank">Hans Frank</a> suggested that Alois's mother had been employed as a housekeeper by a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jewish" title="Jewish">Jewish</a> family in <a href="/wiki/Graz" title="Graz">Graz</a>, and that the family's 19-year-old son Leopold Frankenberger had fathered Alois.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERosenbaum199921_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERosenbaum199921-12">[10]</a></sup> No Frankenberger was registered in Graz during that period, no record has been produced of Leopold Frankenberger's existence,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHamann201050_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHamann201050-13">[11]</a></sup> and Jewish residency in <a href="/wiki/Styria" title="Styria">Styria</a> had been illegal for nearly 400 years and would not become legal again until decades after Alois's birth,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHamann201050_13-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHamann201050-13">[11]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcKale2011147_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcKale2011147-14">[12]</a></sup> so historians dismiss the claim that Alois's father was Jewish.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEToland1992246–247_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEToland1992246–247-15">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKershaw19998–9_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKershaw19998–9-16">[14]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_years">Early years</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Childhood_and_education">Childhood and education</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-1989-0322-506,_Adolf_Hitler,_Kinderbild_retouched.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2048" data-file-width="1400" decoding="async" height="249" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-1989-0322-506%2C_Adolf_Hitler%2C_Kinderbild_retouched.jpg/170px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-1989-0322-506%2C_Adolf_Hitler%2C_Kinderbild_retouched.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-1989-0322-506%2C_Adolf_Hitler%2C_Kinderbild_retouched.jpg/255px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-1989-0322-506%2C_Adolf_Hitler%2C_Kinderbild_retouched.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-1989-0322-506%2C_Adolf_Hitler%2C_Kinderbild_retouched.jpg/340px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-1989-0322-506%2C_Adolf_Hitler%2C_Kinderbild_retouched.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-1989-0322-506,_Adolf_Hitler,_Kinderbild_retouched.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Adolf Hitler as an infant (<abbr title="circa">c.</abbr><span style="white-space:nowrap;"> 1889–90)</span></div></div></div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1096954695/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">.mw-parser-output .tmulti .multiimageinner{display:flex;flex-direction:column}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .theader{clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:center;align-self:center;background-color:transparent;width:100%}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbcaption{background-color:transparent}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-left{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-right{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-center{text-align:center}@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;max-width:none!important;align-items:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{justify-content:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle .thumbcaption{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow>.thumbcaption{text-align:center}}</style><div class="thumb tmulti tleft"><div class="thumbinner multiimageinner" style="width:222px;max-width:222px"><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:115px;max-width:115px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:140px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Alois_Hitler_in_his_last_years.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="540" data-file-width="432" decoding="async" height="141" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Alois_Hitler_in_his_last_years.jpg/113px-Alois_Hitler_in_his_last_years.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Alois_Hitler_in_his_last_years.jpg/170px-Alois_Hitler_in_his_last_years.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Alois_Hitler_in_his_last_years.jpg/226px-Alois_Hitler_in_his_last_years.jpg 2x" width="113"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption text-align-center">Hitler's father, <a href="/wiki/Alois_Hitler" title="Alois Hitler">Alois</a>, <abbr title="circa">c.</abbr><span style="white-space:nowrap;"> 1900</span></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="width:103px;max-width:103px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:140px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Klara_Hitler.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="680" data-file-width="489" decoding="async" height="140" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Klara_Hitler.jpg/101px-Klara_Hitler.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Klara_Hitler.jpg/152px-Klara_Hitler.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Klara_Hitler.jpg/202px-Klara_Hitler.jpg 2x" width="101"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption text-align-center">Hitler's mother, <a href="/wiki/Klara_Hitler" title="Klara Hitler">Klara</a>, 1870s</div></div></div></div></div>
<p>Adolf Hitler was born on 20 April 1889 in <a href="/wiki/Braunau_am_Inn" title="Braunau am Inn">Braunau am Inn</a>, a town in <a href="/wiki/Austria-Hungary" title="Austria-Hungary">Austria-Hungary</a> (in present-day Austria), close to the border with the <a href="/wiki/German_Empire" title="German Empire">German Empire</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHouse_of_Responsibility_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHouse_of_Responsibility-17">[15]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBullock199923_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBullock199923-18">[16]</a></sup> He was the fourth of six children born to Alois Hitler and his third wife, <a href="/wiki/Klara_Hitler" title="Klara Hitler">Klara Pölzl</a>. Three of Hitler's siblings—Gustav, Ida, and Otto—died in infancy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKershaw20084_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKershaw20084-19">[17]</a></sup> Also living in the household were Alois's children from his second marriage: Alois Jr. (born 1882) and <a href="/wiki/Angela_Hitler" title="Angela Hitler">Angela</a> (born 1883).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEToland19766_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEToland19766-20">[18]</a></sup> When Hitler was three, the family moved to <a href="/wiki/Passau" title="Passau">Passau</a>, Germany.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERosmus200433_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERosmus200433-21">[19]</a></sup> There he acquired the distinctive <a href="/wiki/Bavarian_language" title="Bavarian language">lower Bavarian dialect</a>, rather than <a href="/wiki/Austrian_German" title="Austrian German">Austrian German</a>, which marked his speech throughout his life.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKeller201015_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKeller201015-22">[20]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHamann20107–8_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHamann20107–8-23">[21]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKubizek200637_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKubizek200637-24">[22]</a></sup> The family returned to Austria and settled in <a href="/wiki/Leonding" title="Leonding">Leonding</a> in 1894, and in June 1895 Alois retired to Hafeld, near <a href="/wiki/Lambach" title="Lambach">Lambach</a>, where he farmed and kept bees. Hitler attended <span title="German-language text"><i lang="de"><a href="/wiki/Volksschule" title="Volksschule">Volksschule</a></i></span> (a state-funded primary school) in nearby <a href="/wiki/Fischlham" title="Fischlham">Fischlham</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKubizek200692_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKubizek200692-25">[23]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHitler19996_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHitler19996-26">[24]</a></sup>
</p><p>The move to Hafeld coincided with the onset of intense father-son conflicts caused by Hitler's refusal to conform to the strict discipline of his school.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFromm1977493–498_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFromm1977493–498-27">[25]</a></sup> His father beat him, although his mother tried to protect him.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDiver2005_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDiver2005-28">[26]</a></sup> Alois Hitler's farming efforts at Hafeld ended in failure, and in 1897 the family moved to Lambach. The eight-year-old Hitler took singing lessons, sang in the church choir, and even considered becoming a priest.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShirer196010–11_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShirer196010–11-29">[27]</a></sup> In 1898 the family returned permanently to Leonding. Hitler was deeply affected by the death of his younger brother Edmund, who died in 1900 from <a href="/wiki/Measles" title="Measles">measles</a>. Hitler changed from a confident, outgoing, conscientious student to a morose, detached boy who constantly fought with his father and teachers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPayne199022_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPayne199022-30">[28]</a></sup>
</p><p>Alois had made a successful career in the customs bureau and wanted his son to follow in his footsteps.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKershaw20089_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKershaw20089-31">[29]</a></sup> Hitler later dramatised an episode from this period when his father took him to visit a customs office, depicting it as an event that gave rise to an unforgiving antagonism between father and son, who were both strong-willed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHitler19998_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHitler19998-32">[30]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKeller201033–34_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKeller201033–34-33">[31]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFest197732_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFest197732-34">[32]</a></sup> Ignoring his son's desire to attend a classical high school and become an artist, Alois sent Hitler to the <span title="German-language text"><i lang="de"><a href="/wiki/Realschule" title="Realschule">Realschule</a></i></span> in Linz in September 1900.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Realschule_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-Realschule-35">[c]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKershaw20088_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKershaw20088-36">[33]</a></sup> Hitler rebelled against this decision, and in <span title="German-language text"><i lang="de"><a href="/wiki/Mein_Kampf" title="Mein Kampf">Mein Kampf</a></i></span> states that he intentionally did poorly in school, hoping that once his father saw "what little progress I was making at the technical school he would let me devote myself to my dream".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHitler199910_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHitler199910-37">[34]</a></sup>
</p><p>Like many Austrian Germans, Hitler began to develop <a href="/wiki/German_nationalism" title="German nationalism">German nationalist</a> ideas from a young age.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEvans2003163–164_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEvans2003163–164-38">[35]</a></sup> He expressed loyalty only to Germany, despising the declining <a href="/wiki/Habsburg_monarchy" title="Habsburg monarchy">Habsburg monarchy</a> and its rule over an ethnically variegated empire.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBendersky200026_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBendersky200026-39">[36]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERyschka200835_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERyschka200835-40">[37]</a></sup> Hitler and his friends used the greeting "Heil", and sang the "<a href="/wiki/Deutschlandlied" title="Deutschlandlied">Deutschlandlied</a>" instead of the <a href="/wiki/Gott_erhalte_Franz_den_Kaiser#Austria-Hungary" title="Gott erhalte Franz den Kaiser">Austrian Imperial anthem</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHamann201013_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHamann201013-41">[38]</a></sup>
</p><p>After Alois's sudden death on 3 January 1903, Hitler's performance at school deteriorated and his mother allowed him to leave.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKershaw200810_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKershaw200810-42">[39]</a></sup> He enrolled at the <span title="German-language text"><i lang="de">Realschule</i></span> in <a href="/wiki/Steyr" title="Steyr">Steyr</a> in September 1904, where his behaviour and performance improved.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKershaw199919_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKershaw199919-43">[40]</a></sup> In 1905, after passing a repeat of the final exam, Hitler left the school without any ambitions for further education or clear plans for a career.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKershaw199920_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKershaw199920-44">[41]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_adulthood_in_Vienna_and_Munich">Early adulthood in Vienna and Munich</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Paintings_by_Adolf_Hitler" title="Paintings by Adolf Hitler">Paintings by Adolf Hitler</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hitler_house_in_Leonding.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1296" data-file-width="2049" decoding="async" height="139" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Hitler_house_in_Leonding.jpg/220px-Hitler_house_in_Leonding.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Hitler_house_in_Leonding.jpg/330px-Hitler_house_in_Leonding.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Hitler_house_in_Leonding.jpg/440px-Hitler_house_in_Leonding.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hitler_house_in_Leonding.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The house in <a href="/wiki/Leonding" title="Leonding">Leonding, Austria</a> where Hitler spent his early adolescence (photo taken in July 2012)</div></div></div>
<p>In 1907, Hitler left Linz to live and study fine art in <a href="/wiki/Vienna" title="Vienna">Vienna</a>, financed by orphan's benefits and support from his mother. He applied for admission to the <a href="/wiki/Academy_of_Fine_Arts_Vienna" title="Academy of Fine Arts Vienna">Academy of Fine Arts Vienna</a> but was rejected twice.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHitler199920_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHitler199920-45">[42]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBullock196230–31_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBullock196230–31-46">[43]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Rector_(academia)" title="Rector (academia)">director</a> suggested Hitler should apply to the School of Architecture, but he lacked the necessary academic credentials because he had not finished secondary school.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBullock196231_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBullock196231-47">[44]</a></sup>
</p><p>On 21 December 1907, his mother died of <a href="/wiki/Breast_cancer" title="Breast cancer">breast cancer</a> at the age of 47, when he himself was 18. In 1909 Hitler ran out of money and was forced to live a <a href="/wiki/Bohemianism" title="Bohemianism">bohemian</a> life in homeless shelters and <a href="/wiki/Meldemannstra%C3%9Fe_dormitory" title="Meldemannstraße dormitory">a men's dormitory</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBullock199930–33_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBullock199930–33-48">[45]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHamann2010157_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHamann2010157-49">[46]</a></sup> He earned money as a casual labourer and by painting and selling watercolours of Vienna's sights.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHitler199920_45-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHitler199920-45">[42]</a></sup> During his time in Vienna, he pursued a growing passion for architecture and music, attending ten performances of <span title="German-language text"><i lang="de"><a href="/wiki/Lohengrin_(opera)" title="Lohengrin (opera)">Lohengrin</a></i></span>, his favourite <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wagner" title="Wagner">Wagner</a> opera.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKershaw199941,_42_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKershaw199941,_42-50">[47]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Adolf_Hitler_Der_Alte_Hof.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1656" data-file-width="2301" decoding="async" height="158" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Adolf_Hitler_Der_Alte_Hof.jpg/220px-Adolf_Hitler_Der_Alte_Hof.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Adolf_Hitler_Der_Alte_Hof.jpg/330px-Adolf_Hitler_Der_Alte_Hof.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Adolf_Hitler_Der_Alte_Hof.jpg/440px-Adolf_Hitler_Der_Alte_Hof.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Adolf_Hitler_Der_Alte_Hof.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Courtyard_of_the_Old_Residency_in_Munich" title="The Courtyard of the Old Residency in Munich">The Alter Hof in Munich</a></i>. Watercolour by Adolf Hitler, 1914</div></div></div>
<p>It was in Vienna that Hitler first became exposed to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Racist" title="Racist">racist</a> rhetoric.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShirer196026_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShirer196026-51">[48]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Populists" title="Populists">Populists</a> such as mayor <a href="/wiki/Karl_Lueger" title="Karl Lueger">Karl Lueger</a> exploited the climate of virulent <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anti-Semitism" title="Anti-Semitism">anti-Semitism</a> and occasionally espoused German nationalist notions for political effect. German nationalism had a particularly widespread following in the <a href="/wiki/Mariahilf" title="Mariahilf">Mariahilf</a> district, where Hitler lived.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHamann2010243–246_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHamann2010243–246-52">[49]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Georg_Ritter_von_Sch%C3%B6nerer" title="Georg Ritter von Schönerer">Georg Ritter von Schönerer</a> became a major influence on Hitler.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENicholls2000236,_237,_274_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENicholls2000236,_237,_274-53">[50]</a></sup> He also developed an admiration for <a href="/wiki/Martin_Luther" title="Martin Luther">Martin Luther</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHamann2010250_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHamann2010250-54">[51]</a></sup> Hitler read local newspapers such as <i><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Deutsches_Volksblatt&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Deutsches Volksblatt (page does not exist)">Deutsches Volksblatt</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> [<a class="extiw" href="https://de.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deutsches_Volksblatt" title="de:Deutsches Volksblatt">de</a>]</span></i> that fanned prejudice and played on Christian fears of being swamped by an influx of Eastern European Jews.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHamann2010341–345_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHamann2010341–345-55">[52]</a></sup> He read newspapers and pamphlets that published the thoughts of philosophers and theoreticians such as <a href="/wiki/Houston_Stewart_Chamberlain" title="Houston Stewart Chamberlain">Houston Stewart Chamberlain</a>, <a href="/wiki/Charles_Darwin" title="Charles Darwin">Charles Darwin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Friedrich_Nietzsche" title="Friedrich Nietzsche">Friedrich Nietzsche</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gustave_Le_Bon" title="Gustave Le Bon">Gustave Le Bon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Schopenhauer" title="Arthur Schopenhauer">Arthur Schopenhauer</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHamann2010233_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHamann2010233-56">[53]</a></sup>
</p><p>The origin and development of Hitler's anti-Semitism remains a matter of debate.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKershaw199960–67_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKershaw199960–67-57">[54]</a></sup> His friend, <a href="/wiki/August_Kubizek" title="August Kubizek">August Kubizek</a>, claimed that Hitler was a "confirmed anti-Semite" before he left Linz.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShirer196025_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShirer196025-58">[55]</a></sup> However, historian Brigitte Hamann describes Kubizek's claim as "problematical".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHamann201058_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHamann201058-59">[56]</a></sup> While Hitler states in <span title="German-language text"><i lang="de">Mein Kampf</i></span> that he first became an anti-Semite in Vienna,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHitler199952_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHitler199952-60">[57]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Reinhold_Hanisch" title="Reinhold Hanisch">Reinhold Hanisch</a>, who helped him sell his paintings, disagrees. Hitler had dealings with Jews while living in Vienna.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEToland199245_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEToland199245-61">[58]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKershaw199955,_63_62-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKershaw199955,_63-62">[59]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHamann2010174_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHamann2010174-63">[60]</a></sup> Historian <a href="/wiki/Richard_J._Evans" title="Richard J. Evans">Richard J. Evans</a> states that "historians now generally agree that his notorious, murderous anti-Semitism emerged well after Germany's defeat [in World War I], as a product of the paranoid <a href="/wiki/Stab-in-the-back_myth" title="Stab-in-the-back myth">"stab-in-the-back" explanation</a> for the catastrophe".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEvans2011_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEvans2011-64">[61]</a></sup>
</p><p>Hitler received the final part of his father's estate in May 1913 and moved to <a href="/wiki/Munich" title="Munich">Munich</a>, Germany.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShirer196027_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShirer196027-65">[62]</a></sup> When he was conscripted into the <a href="/wiki/Austro-Hungarian_Army" title="Austro-Hungarian Army">Austro-Hungarian Army</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWeber201013_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWeber201013-66">[63]</a></sup> he journeyed to <a href="/wiki/Salzburg" title="Salzburg">Salzburg</a> on 5 February 1914 for medical assessment. After he was deemed unfit for service, he returned to Munich.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKershaw199986_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKershaw199986-67">[64]</a></sup> Hitler later claimed that he did not wish to serve the <a href="/wiki/Austria-Hungary" title="Austria-Hungary">Habsburg Empire</a> because of the mixture of races in its army and his belief that the collapse of Austria-Hungary was imminent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKershaw199949_68-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKershaw199949-68">[65]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="World_War_I">World War I</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Military_career_of_Adolf_Hitler" title="Military career of Adolf Hitler">Military career of Adolf Hitler</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:292px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-1974-082-44,_Adolf_Hitler_im_Ersten_Weltkrieg_retouched.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="532" data-file-width="686" decoding="async" height="225" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-1974-082-44%2C_Adolf_Hitler_im_Ersten_Weltkrieg_retouched.jpg/290px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-1974-082-44%2C_Adolf_Hitler_im_Ersten_Weltkrieg_retouched.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-1974-082-44%2C_Adolf_Hitler_im_Ersten_Weltkrieg_retouched.jpg/435px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-1974-082-44%2C_Adolf_Hitler_im_Ersten_Weltkrieg_retouched.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-1974-082-44%2C_Adolf_Hitler_im_Ersten_Weltkrieg_retouched.jpg/580px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-1974-082-44%2C_Adolf_Hitler_im_Ersten_Weltkrieg_retouched.jpg 2x" width="290"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-1974-082-44,_Adolf_Hitler_im_Ersten_Weltkrieg_retouched.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Hitler (far right, seated) with his army comrades of the Bavarian Reserve Infantry Regiment<span class="nowrap"> </span>16 (<abbr title="circa">c.</abbr><span style="white-space:nowrap;"> 1914–18)</span></div></div></div>
<p>In August 1914, at the outbreak of <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>, Hitler was living in Munich and voluntarily enlisted in the <a href="/wiki/Bavarian_Army" title="Bavarian Army">Bavarian Army</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKershaw199990_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKershaw199990-69">[66]</a></sup> According to a 1924 report by the Bavarian authorities, allowing Hitler to serve was almost certainly an administrative error, since as an Austrian citizen, he should have been returned to Austria.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKershaw199990_69-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKershaw199990-69">[66]</a></sup> Posted to the <a href="/wiki/6th_Bavarian_Reserve_Division" title="6th Bavarian Reserve Division">Bavarian Reserve Infantry Regiment 16</a> (1st Company of the List Regiment),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWeber201012–13_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWeber201012–13-70">[67]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKershaw199990_69-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKershaw199990-69">[66]</a></sup> he served as a dispatch <a href="/wiki/Runner_(soldier)" title="Runner (soldier)">runner</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Western_Front_(World_War_I)" title="Western Front (World War I)">Western Front</a> in France and Belgium,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKershaw200853_71-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKershaw200853-71">[68]</a></sup> spending nearly half his time at the regimental headquarters in <a href="/wiki/Fournes-en-Weppes" title="Fournes-en-Weppes">Fournes-en-Weppes</a>, well behind the front lines.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKershaw200854_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKershaw200854-72">[69]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWeber2010100_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWeber2010100-73">[70]</a></sup> He was present at the <a href="/wiki/First_Battle_of_Ypres" title="First Battle of Ypres">First Battle of Ypres</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Somme" title="Battle of the Somme">Battle of the Somme</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Arras_(1917)" title="Battle of Arras (1917)">Battle of Arras</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Passchendaele" title="Battle of Passchendaele">Battle of Passchendaele</a>, and was wounded at the Somme.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShirer196030_74-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShirer196030-74">[71]</a></sup> He was decorated for bravery, receiving the <a href="/wiki/Iron_Cross" title="Iron Cross">Iron Cross</a>, Second Class, in 1914.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShirer196030_74-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShirer196030-74">[71]</a></sup> On a recommendation by Lieutenant <a href="/wiki/Hugo_Gutmann" title="Hugo Gutmann">Hugo Gutmann</a>, Hitler's Jewish superior, he received the Iron Cross, First Class on 4 August 1918, a decoration rarely awarded to one of Hitler's <span title="German-language text"><i lang="de"><a href="/wiki/Gefreiter" title="Gefreiter">Gefreiter</a></i></span> rank.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKershaw200859_75-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKershaw200859-75">[72]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWeber2010a_76-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWeber2010a-76">[73]</a></sup> He received the <a href="/wiki/Wound_Badge" title="Wound Badge">Black Wound Badge</a> on 18 May 1918.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESteiner1976392_77-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESteiner1976392-77">[74]</a></sup>
</p><p>During his service at headquarters, Hitler pursued his artwork, drawing cartoons and instructions for an army newspaper. During the Battle of the Somme in October 1916, he was wounded in the left thigh when a shell exploded in the dispatch runners' dugout.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKershaw200857_78-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKershaw200857-78">[75]</a></sup> Hitler spent almost two months in hospital at <a href="/wiki/Beelitz" title="Beelitz">Beelitz</a>, returning to his regiment on 5 March 1917.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKershaw200858_79-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKershaw200858-79">[76]</a></sup> On 15 October 1918, he was temporarily blinded in a <a href="/wiki/Mustard_gas" title="Mustard gas">mustard gas</a> attack and was hospitalised in <a href="/wiki/Pasewalk" title="Pasewalk">Pasewalk</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKershaw200859,_60_80-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKershaw200859,_60-80">[77]</a></sup> While there, Hitler learned of Germany's defeat, and—by his own account—upon receiving this news, he suffered a second bout of blindness.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKershaw199997,_102_81-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKershaw199997,_102-81">[78]</a></sup>
</p><p>Hitler described the war as "the greatest of all experiences", and was praised by his commanding officers for his bravery.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKeegan1987238–240_82-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKeegan1987238–240-82">[79]</a></sup> His wartime experience reinforced his German patriotism and he was shocked by Germany's capitulation in November 1918.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBullock196260_83-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBullock196260-83">[80]</a></sup> His bitterness over the collapse of the war effort began to shape his ideology.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKershaw200861,_62_84-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKershaw200861,_62-84">[81]</a></sup> Like other German nationalists, he believed the <span title="German-language text"><i lang="de">Dolchstoßlegende</i></span> (<a href="/wiki/Stab-in-the-back_myth" title="Stab-in-the-back myth">stab-in-the-back myth</a>), which claimed that the German army, "undefeated in the field", had been "stabbed in the back" on the <a href="/wiki/Home_front" title="Home front">home front</a> by civilian leaders, Jews, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marxists" title="Marxists">Marxists</a>, and those who signed the <a href="/wiki/Armistice_of_11_November_1918" title="Armistice of 11 November 1918">armistice</a> that ended the fighting—later dubbed the "November criminals".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKershaw200861–63_85-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKershaw200861–63-85">[82]</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Versailles" title="Treaty of Versailles">Treaty of Versailles</a> stipulated that Germany had to relinquish several of its territories and <a href="/wiki/Demilitarisation" title="Demilitarisation">demilitarise</a> the <a href="/wiki/Rhineland" title="Rhineland">Rhineland</a>. The treaty imposed economic sanctions and levied heavy reparations on the country. Many Germans saw the treaty as an unjust humiliation. They especially objected to <a href="/wiki/Article_231_of_the_Treaty_of_Versailles" title="Article 231 of the Treaty of Versailles">Article 231</a>, which they interpreted as declaring Germany responsible for the war.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKershaw200896_86-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKershaw200896-86">[83]</a></sup> The Versailles Treaty and the economic, social, and political conditions in Germany after the war were later exploited by Hitler for political gain.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKershaw200880,_90,_92_87-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKershaw200880,_90,_92-87">[84]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Entry_into_politics">Entry into politics</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Political_views_of_Adolf_Hitler" title="Political views of Adolf Hitler">Political views of Adolf Hitler</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hitler%27s_DAP_membership_card.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="409" data-file-width="612" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Hitler%27s_DAP_membership_card.png/220px-Hitler%27s_DAP_membership_card.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Hitler%27s_DAP_membership_card.png/330px-Hitler%27s_DAP_membership_card.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Hitler%27s_DAP_membership_card.png/440px-Hitler%27s_DAP_membership_card.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hitler%27s_DAP_membership_card.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Hitler's <a href="/wiki/German_Workers%27_Party" title="German Workers' Party">German Workers' Party</a> (DAP) membership card</div></div></div>
<p>After World War I, Hitler returned to Munich.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBullock199961_88-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBullock199961-88">[85]</a></sup> Without formal education or career prospects, he remained in the army.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKershaw1999109_89-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKershaw1999109-89">[86]</a></sup> In July 1919 he was appointed <span title="German-language text"><i lang="de">Verbindungsmann</i></span> (intelligence agent) of an <span title="German-language text"><i lang="de">Aufklärungskommando</i></span> (reconnaissance unit) of the <span title="German-language text"><i lang="de"><a href="/wiki/Reichswehr" title="Reichswehr">Reichswehr</a></i></span>, assigned to influence other soldiers and to infiltrate the <a href="/wiki/German_Workers%27_Party" title="German Workers' Party">German Workers' Party</a> (DAP). At a DAP meeting on 12 September 1919, Party Chairman <a href="/wiki/Anton_Drexler" title="Anton Drexler">Anton Drexler</a> was impressed with Hitler's oratorical skills. He gave him a copy of his pamphlet <i>My Political Awakening</i>, which contained anti-Semitic, nationalist, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anti-capitalist" title="Anti-capitalist">anti-capitalist</a>, and anti-Marxist ideas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKershaw200882_90-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKershaw200882-90">[87]</a></sup> On the orders of his army superiors, Hitler applied to join the party,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEvans2003170_91-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEvans2003170-91">[88]</a></sup> and within a week was accepted as party member 555 (the party began counting membership at 500 to give the impression they were a much larger party).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKershaw200875,_76_92-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKershaw200875,_76-92">[89]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMitcham199667_93-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMitcham199667-93">[90]</a></sup>
</p><p>Hitler made his earliest known written statement about the <a href="/wiki/Jewish_question" title="Jewish question">Jewish question</a> in a 16 September 1919 letter to Adolf Gemlich (now known as the <a href="/wiki/Gemlich_letter" title="Gemlich letter">Gemlich letter</a>). In the letter, Hitler argues that the aim of the government "must unshakably be the removal of the Jews altogether".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKershaw1999125–126_94-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKershaw1999125–126-94">[91]</a></sup>
</p><p>At the DAP, Hitler met <a href="/wiki/Dietrich_Eckart" title="Dietrich Eckart">Dietrich Eckart</a>, one of the party's founders and a member of the occult <a href="/wiki/Thule_Society" title="Thule Society">Thule Society</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFest197021_95-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFest197021-95">[92]</a></sup> Eckart became Hitler's mentor, exchanging ideas with him and introducing him to a wide range of Munich society.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKershaw200894,_95,_100_96-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKershaw200894,_95,_100-96">[93]</a></sup> To increase its appeal, the DAP changed its name to the <span title="German-language text"><i lang="de">Nationalsozialistische Deutsche Arbeiterpartei</i></span> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Socialist_German_Workers%27_Party" title="National Socialist German Workers' Party">National Socialist German Workers' Party</a> (NSDAP), known colloquially as the "Nazi Party").<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKershaw200887_97-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKershaw200887-97">[94]</a></sup> Hitler designed the party's banner of a <a href="/wiki/Swastika" title="Swastika">swastika</a> in a white circle on a red background.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKershaw200888_98-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKershaw200888-98">[95]</a></sup>
</p><p>Hitler was discharged from the army on 31 March 1920 and began working full-time for the party.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKershaw200893_99-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKershaw200893-99">[96]</a></sup> The party headquarters was in Munich, a hotbed of anti-government German nationalists determined to crush Marxism and undermine the <a href="/wiki/Weimar_Republic" title="Weimar Republic">Weimar Republic</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKershaw200881_100-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKershaw200881-100">[97]</a></sup> In February 1921—already highly effective at <a href="/wiki/Crowd_manipulation" title="Crowd manipulation">crowd manipulation</a>—he spoke to a crowd of over 6,000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKershaw200889_101-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKershaw200889-101">[98]</a></sup> To publicise the meeting, two truckloads of party supporters drove around Munich waving swastika flags and distributing leaflets. Hitler soon gained notoriety for his rowdy <a href="/wiki/Polemic" title="Polemic">polemic</a> speeches against the Treaty of Versailles, rival politicians, and especially against Marxists and Jews.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKershaw200889–92_102-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKershaw200889–92-102">[99]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_102-10460,_Adolf_Hitler,_Rednerposen.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="624" data-file-width="800" decoding="async" height="172" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Bundesarchiv_Bild_102-10460%2C_Adolf_Hitler%2C_Rednerposen.jpg/220px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_102-10460%2C_Adolf_Hitler%2C_Rednerposen.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Bundesarchiv_Bild_102-10460%2C_Adolf_Hitler%2C_Rednerposen.jpg/330px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_102-10460%2C_Adolf_Hitler%2C_Rednerposen.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Bundesarchiv_Bild_102-10460%2C_Adolf_Hitler%2C_Rednerposen.jpg/440px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_102-10460%2C_Adolf_Hitler%2C_Rednerposen.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_102-10460,_Adolf_Hitler,_Rednerposen.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Hitler poses for the camera, 1930</div></div></div>
<p>In June 1921, while Hitler and Eckart were on a fundraising trip to <a href="/wiki/Berlin" title="Berlin">Berlin</a>, a mutiny broke out within the Nazi Party in Munich. Members of its executive committee wanted to merge with the Nuremberg-based <a href="/wiki/German_Socialist_Party" title="German Socialist Party">German Socialist Party</a> (DSP).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKershaw2008100,_101_103-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKershaw2008100,_101-103">[100]</a></sup> Hitler returned to Munich on 11 July and angrily tendered his resignation. The committee members realised that the resignation of their leading public figure and speaker would mean the end of the party.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKershaw2008102_104-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKershaw2008102-104">[101]</a></sup> Hitler announced he would rejoin on the condition that he would replace Drexler as party chairman, and that the party headquarters would remain in Munich.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKershaw2008103_105-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKershaw2008103-105">[102]</a></sup> The committee agreed, and he rejoined the party on 26 July as member 3,680. Hitler continued to face some opposition within the Nazi Party. Opponents of Hitler in the leadership had <a href="/wiki/Hermann_Esser" title="Hermann Esser">Hermann Esser</a> expelled from the party, and they printed 3,000 copies of a pamphlet attacking Hitler as a traitor to the party.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKershaw2008103_105-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKershaw2008103-105">[102]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-libel_suit_106-0"><a href="#cite_note-libel_suit-106">[d]</a></sup> In the following days, Hitler spoke to several packed houses and defended himself and Esser, to thunderous applause. His strategy proved successful, and at a special party congress on 29 July, he was granted absolute powers as party chairman, replacing Drexler, by a vote of 533<span class="nowrap"> </span>to<span class="nowrap"> </span>1.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKershaw200883,_103_107-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKershaw200883,_103-107">[103]</a></sup>
</p><p>Hitler's vitriolic beer hall speeches began attracting regular audiences. A <a href="/wiki/Demagogue" title="Demagogue">demagogue</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKershaw2000bxv_108-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKershaw2000bxv-108">[104]</a></sup> he became adept at using populist themes, including the use of <a href="/wiki/Scapegoat" title="Scapegoat">scapegoats</a>, who were blamed for his listeners' economic hardships.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBullock1999376_109-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBullock1999376-109">[105]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFrauenfeld1937_110-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFrauenfeld1937-110">[106]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGoebbels1936_111-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGoebbels1936-111">[107]</a></sup> Hitler used personal magnetism and an understanding of crowd psychology to his advantage while engaged in public speaking.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKershaw2008105–106_112-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKershaw2008105–106-112">[108]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBullock1999377_113-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBullock1999377-113">[109]</a></sup> Historians have noted the hypnotic effect of his rhetoric on large audiences, and of his eyes in small groups.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKressel2002121_114-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKressel2002121-114">[110]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Alfons_Heck" title="Alfons Heck">Alfons Heck</a>, a former member of the Hitler Youth, recalled:
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r996844942">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>We erupted into a frenzy of nationalistic pride that bordered on hysteria. For minutes on end, we shouted at the top of our lungs, with tears streaming down our faces: <span title="German-language text"><i lang="de">Sieg Heil, Sieg Heil, Sieg Heil!</i></span> From that moment on, I belonged to Adolf Hitler body and soul.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHeck200123_115-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHeck200123-115">[111]</a></sup></p></blockquote>
<p>Early followers included <a href="/wiki/Rudolf_Hess" title="Rudolf Hess">Rudolf Hess</a>, former air force ace <a href="/wiki/Hermann_G%C3%B6ring" title="Hermann Göring">Hermann Göring</a>, and army captain <a href="/wiki/Ernst_R%C3%B6hm" title="Ernst Röhm">Ernst Röhm</a>. Röhm became head of the Nazis' paramilitary organisation, the <span title="German-language text"><i lang="de"><a href="/wiki/Sturmabteilung" title="Sturmabteilung">Sturmabteilung</a></i></span> (SA, "Stormtroopers"), which protected meetings and attacked political opponents. A critical influence on Hitler's thinking during this period was the <span title="German-language text"><i lang="de"><a href="/wiki/Aufbau_Vereinigung" title="Aufbau Vereinigung">Aufbau Vereinigung</a></i></span>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKellogg2005275_116-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKellogg2005275-116">[112]</a></sup> a conspiratorial group of <a href="/wiki/White_%C3%A9migr%C3%A9" title="White émigré">White Russian</a> exiles and early Nazis. The group, financed with funds channelled from wealthy industrialists, introduced Hitler to the idea of a Jewish conspiracy, linking international finance with <a href="/wiki/Bolshevism" title="Bolshevism">Bolshevism</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKellogg2005203_117-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKellogg2005203-117">[113]</a></sup>
</p><p>The programme of the Nazi Party was laid out in their <a href="/wiki/National_Socialist_Program" title="National Socialist Program">25-point programme</a> on 24 February 1920. This did not represent a coherent ideology, but was a conglomeration of received ideas which had currency in the <span title="German-language text"><i lang="de"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/V%C3%B6lkisch" title="Völkisch">völkisch</a></i></span> <a href="/wiki/Pan-Germanism" title="Pan-Germanism">Pan-Germanic</a> movement, such as <a href="/wiki/Ultranationalism" title="Ultranationalism">ultranationalism</a>, opposition to the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Versailles" title="Treaty of Versailles">Treaty of Versailles</a>, distrust of <a href="/wiki/Capitalism" title="Capitalism">capitalism</a>, as well as some <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Socialist" title="Socialist">socialist</a> ideas. For Hitler, though, the most important aspect of it was its strong <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anti-Semitic" title="Anti-Semitic">anti-Semitic</a> stance. He also perceived the programme as primarily a basis for propaganda and for attracting people to the party.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBracher1970115–116_118-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBracher1970115–116-118">[114]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Beer_Hall_Putsch_and_Landsberg_Prison">Beer Hall Putsch and Landsberg Prison</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Beer_Hall_Putsch" title="Beer Hall Putsch">Beer Hall Putsch</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_102-00344A,_M%C3%BCnchen,_nach_Hitler-Ludendorff_Prozess.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1224" data-file-width="1682" decoding="async" height="160" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Bundesarchiv_Bild_102-00344A%2C_M%C3%BCnchen%2C_nach_Hitler-Ludendorff_Prozess.jpg/220px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_102-00344A%2C_M%C3%BCnchen%2C_nach_Hitler-Ludendorff_Prozess.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Bundesarchiv_Bild_102-00344A%2C_M%C3%BCnchen%2C_nach_Hitler-Ludendorff_Prozess.jpg/330px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_102-00344A%2C_M%C3%BCnchen%2C_nach_Hitler-Ludendorff_Prozess.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Bundesarchiv_Bild_102-00344A%2C_M%C3%BCnchen%2C_nach_Hitler-Ludendorff_Prozess.jpg/440px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_102-00344A%2C_M%C3%BCnchen%2C_nach_Hitler-Ludendorff_Prozess.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_102-00344A,_M%C3%BCnchen,_nach_Hitler-Ludendorff_Prozess.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Defendants in the Beer Hall Putsch trial, 1 April 1924. From left to right: <a href="/wiki/Heinz_Pernet" title="Heinz Pernet">Heinz Pernet</a>, <a href="/wiki/Friedrich_Weber_(veterinarian)" title="Friedrich Weber (veterinarian)">Friedrich Weber</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wilhelm_Frick" title="Wilhelm Frick">Wilhelm Frick</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hermann_Kriebel" title="Hermann Kriebel">Hermann Kriebel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Erich_Ludendorff" title="Erich Ludendorff">Erich Ludendorff</a>, Hitler, <a href="/wiki/Wilhelm_Br%C3%BCckner" title="Wilhelm Brückner">Wilhelm Brückner</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ernst_R%C3%B6hm" title="Ernst Röhm">Ernst Röhm</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Robert_Heinrich_Wagner" title="Robert Heinrich Wagner">Robert Wagner</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>In 1923, Hitler enlisted the help of World War I General <a href="/wiki/Erich_Ludendorff" title="Erich Ludendorff">Erich Ludendorff</a> for an attempted coup known as the "<a href="/wiki/Beer_Hall_Putsch" title="Beer Hall Putsch">Beer Hall Putsch</a>". The Nazi Party used <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Italian_Fascism" title="Italian Fascism">Italian Fascism</a> as a model for their appearance and policies. Hitler wanted to emulate <a href="/wiki/Benito_Mussolini" title="Benito Mussolini">Benito Mussolini</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/March_on_Rome" title="March on Rome">March on Rome</a>" of 1922 by staging his own coup in Bavaria, to be followed by a challenge to the government in Berlin. Hitler and Ludendorff sought the support of <span title="German-language text"><i lang="de">Staatskommissar</i></span> (State Commissioner) <a href="/wiki/Gustav_Ritter_von_Kahr" title="Gustav Ritter von Kahr">Gustav Ritter von Kahr</a>, Bavaria's <i>de facto</i> ruler. However, Kahr, along with Police Chief <a href="/wiki/Hans_Ritter_von_Seisser" title="Hans Ritter von Seisser">Hans Ritter von Seisser</a> and Reichswehr General <a href="/wiki/Otto_von_Lossow" title="Otto von Lossow">Otto von Lossow</a>, wanted to install a nationalist dictatorship without Hitler.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKershaw2008126_119-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKershaw2008126-119">[115]</a></sup>
</p><p>On 8 November 1923, Hitler and the SA stormed a public meeting of 3,000 people organised by Kahr in the <a href="/wiki/B%C3%BCrgerbr%C3%A4ukeller" title="Bürgerbräukeller">Bürgerbräukeller</a>, a beer hall in Munich. Interrupting Kahr's speech, he announced that the national revolution had begun and declared the formation of a new government with Ludendorff.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKershaw2008128_120-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKershaw2008128-120">[116]</a></sup> Retiring to a back room, Hitler, with handgun drawn, demanded and got the support of Kahr, Seisser, and Lossow.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKershaw2008128_120-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKershaw2008128-120">[116]</a></sup> Hitler's forces initially succeeded in occupying the local Reichswehr and police headquarters, but Kahr and his cohorts quickly withdrew their support. Neither the army, nor the state police, joined forces with Hitler.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKershaw2008129_121-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKershaw2008129-121">[117]</a></sup> The next day, Hitler and his followers marched from the beer hall to the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_War_(Kingdom_of_Bavaria)" title="Ministry of War (Kingdom of Bavaria)">Bavarian War Ministry</a> to overthrow the Bavarian government, but police dispersed them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKershaw2008130–131_122-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKershaw2008130–131-122">[118]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_Nazis_who_died_in_the_Beer_Hall_Putsch" title="List of Nazis who died in the Beer Hall Putsch">Sixteen Nazi Party members</a> and four police officers were killed in the failed coup.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShirer196073–74_123-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShirer196073–74-123">[119]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mein_Kampf_dust_jacket.jpeg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="681" data-file-width="617" decoding="async" height="243" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Mein_Kampf_dust_jacket.jpeg/220px-Mein_Kampf_dust_jacket.jpeg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Mein_Kampf_dust_jacket.jpeg/330px-Mein_Kampf_dust_jacket.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Mein_Kampf_dust_jacket.jpeg/440px-Mein_Kampf_dust_jacket.jpeg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mein_Kampf_dust_jacket.jpeg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Dust_jacket" title="Dust jacket">Dust jacket</a> of <span title="German-language text"><i lang="de"><a href="/wiki/Mein_Kampf" title="Mein Kampf">Mein Kampf</a></i></span> (1926–28 edition)</div></div></div>
<p>Hitler fled to the home of <a href="/wiki/Ernst_Hanfstaengl" title="Ernst Hanfstaengl">Ernst Hanfstaengl</a> and by some accounts contemplated suicide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKershaw2008132_124-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKershaw2008132-124">[120]</a></sup> He was depressed but calm when arrested on 11 November 1923 for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/High_treason" title="High treason">high treason</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKershaw2008131_125-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKershaw2008131-125">[121]</a></sup> His trial before the special <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Court_(Bavaria)" title="People's Court (Bavaria)">People's Court</a> in Munich began in February 1924,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMunich_Court,_1924_126-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMunich_Court,_1924-126">[122]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Alfred_Rosenberg" title="Alfred Rosenberg">Alfred Rosenberg</a> became temporary leader of the Nazi Party. On 1 April, Hitler was sentenced to five years' imprisonment at <a href="/wiki/Landsberg_Prison" title="Landsberg Prison">Landsberg Prison</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFulda200968–69_127-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFulda200968–69-127">[123]</a></sup> There, he received friendly treatment from the guards, and was allowed mail from supporters and regular visits by party comrades. Pardoned by the Bavarian Supreme Court, he was released from jail on 20 December 1924, against the state prosecutor's objections.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKershaw1999239_128-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKershaw1999239-128">[124]</a></sup> Including time on remand, Hitler served just over one year in prison.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBullock1962121_129-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBullock1962121-129">[125]</a></sup>
</p><p>While at Landsberg, Hitler dictated most of the first volume of <i>Mein Kampf</i> (<i>My Struggle</i>; originally entitled <i>Four and a Half Years of Struggle against Lies, Stupidity, and Cowardice</i>) at first to his chauffeur, <a href="/wiki/Emil_Maurice" title="Emil Maurice">Emil Maurice</a>, and then to his deputy, <a href="/wiki/Rudolf_Hess" title="Rudolf Hess">Rudolf Hess</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBullock1962121_129-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBullock1962121-129">[125]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKershaw2008147_130-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKershaw2008147-130">[126]</a></sup> The book, dedicated to Thule Society member Dietrich Eckart, was an autobiography and exposition of his ideology. The book laid out Hitler's plans for transforming German society into one based on race. Throughout the book, Jews are equated with "germs" and presented as the "international poisoners" of society. According to Hitler's ideology, the only solution was their extermination. While Hitler did not describe exactly how this was to be accomplished, his "inherent genocidal thrust is undeniable", according to <a href="/wiki/Ian_Kershaw" title="Ian Kershaw">Ian Kershaw</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKershaw2008148–150_131-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKershaw2008148–150-131">[127]</a></sup>
</p><p>Published in two volumes in 1925 and 1926, <span title="German-language text"><i lang="de">Mein Kampf</i></span> sold 228,000 copies between 1925 and 1932. One million copies were sold in 1933, Hitler's first year in office.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShirer196080–81_132-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShirer196080–81-132">[128]</a></sup>
</p><p>Shortly before Hitler was eligible for parole, the Bavarian government attempted to have him deported to Austria.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKershaw1999237_133-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKershaw1999237-133">[129]</a></sup> The Austrian federal chancellor rejected the request on the specious grounds that his service in the German Army made his Austrian citizenship void.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKershaw1999238_134-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKershaw1999238-134">[130]</a></sup> In response, Hitler formally renounced his Austrian citizenship on 7 April 1925.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKershaw1999238_134-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKershaw1999238-134">[130]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rebuilding_the_Nazi_Party">Rebuilding the Nazi Party</span></h3>
<p>At the time of Hitler's release from prison, politics in Germany had become less combative and the economy had improved, limiting Hitler's opportunities for political agitation. As a result of the failed Beer Hall Putsch, the Nazi Party and its affiliated organisations were banned in Bavaria. In a meeting with the Prime Minister of Bavaria <a href="/wiki/Heinrich_Held" title="Heinrich Held">Heinrich Held</a> on 4 January 1925, Hitler agreed to respect the state's authority and promised that he would seek political power only through the democratic process. The meeting paved the way for the ban on the Nazi Party to be lifted on 16 February.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKershaw2008158,_161,_162_135-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKershaw2008158,_161,_162-135">[131]</a></sup> However, after an inflammatory speech he gave on 27 February, Hitler was barred from public speaking by the Bavarian authorities, a ban that remained in place until 1927.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKershaw2008162,_166_136-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKershaw2008162,_166-136">[132]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShirer1960129_137-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShirer1960129-137">[133]</a></sup> To advance his political ambitions in spite of the ban, Hitler appointed <a href="/wiki/Gregor_Strasser" title="Gregor Strasser">Gregor Strasser</a>, <a href="/wiki/Otto_Strasser" title="Otto Strasser">Otto Strasser</a> and <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Goebbels" title="Joseph Goebbels">Joseph Goebbels</a> to organise and enlarge the Nazi Party in northern Germany. Gregor Strasser steered a more independent political course, emphasising the socialist elements of the party's programme.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKershaw2008166,_167_138-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKershaw2008166,_167-138">[134]</a></sup>
</p><p>The stock market in the United States <a href="/wiki/Wall_Street_Crash_of_1929" title="Wall Street Crash of 1929">crashed on 24 October 1929</a>. The impact in Germany was dire: millions were thrown out of work and several major banks collapsed. Hitler and the Nazi Party prepared to take advantage of the emergency to gain support for their party. They promised to repudiate the Versailles Treaty, strengthen the economy, and provide jobs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShirer1960136–137_139-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShirer1960136–137-139">[135]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Rise_to_power">Rise to power</span></h2>

<h3><span id="Br.C3.BCning_administration"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Brüning_administration">Brüning administration</span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Great_Depression" title="Great Depression">Great Depression</a> provided a political opportunity for Hitler. Germans were ambivalent about the <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_republic" title="Parliamentary republic">parliamentary republic</a>, which faced challenges from right- and left-wing extremists. The moderate political parties were increasingly unable to stem the tide of extremism, and the <a href="/wiki/1929_German_referendum" title="1929 German referendum">German referendum of 1929</a> helped to elevate Nazi ideology.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKolb1988105_141-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKolb1988105-141">[137]</a></sup> The elections of September 1930 resulted in the break-up of a <a href="/wiki/Grand_coalition" title="Grand coalition">grand coalition</a> and its replacement with a minority cabinet. Its leader, chancellor <a href="/wiki/Heinrich_Br%C3%BCning" title="Heinrich Brüning">Heinrich Brüning</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Centre_Party_(Germany)" title="Centre Party (Germany)">Centre Party</a>, governed through <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Emergency_powers" title="Emergency powers">emergency decrees</a> from President <a href="/wiki/Paul_von_Hindenburg" title="Paul von Hindenburg">Paul von Hindenburg</a>. Governance by decree became the new norm and paved the way for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Authoritarian" title="Authoritarian">authoritarian</a> forms of government.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHalperin1965403_''et._seq''_142-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHalperin1965403_''et._seq''-142">[138]</a></sup> The Nazi Party rose from obscurity to win 18.3 per cent of the vote and 107 parliamentary seats in the 1930 election, becoming the second-largest party in parliament.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHalperin1965434–446_''et._seq''_143-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHalperin1965434–446_''et._seq''-143">[139]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_119-0289,_M%C3%BCnchen,_Hitler_bei_Einweihung_%22Braunes_Haus%22.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="580" data-file-width="792" decoding="async" height="161" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Bundesarchiv_Bild_119-0289%2C_M%C3%BCnchen%2C_Hitler_bei_Einweihung_%22Braunes_Haus%22.jpg/220px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_119-0289%2C_M%C3%BCnchen%2C_Hitler_bei_Einweihung_%22Braunes_Haus%22.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Bundesarchiv_Bild_119-0289%2C_M%C3%BCnchen%2C_Hitler_bei_Einweihung_%22Braunes_Haus%22.jpg/330px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_119-0289%2C_M%C3%BCnchen%2C_Hitler_bei_Einweihung_%22Braunes_Haus%22.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Bundesarchiv_Bild_119-0289%2C_M%C3%BCnchen%2C_Hitler_bei_Einweihung_%22Braunes_Haus%22.jpg/440px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_119-0289%2C_M%C3%BCnchen%2C_Hitler_bei_Einweihung_%22Braunes_Haus%22.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_119-0289,_M%C3%BCnchen,_Hitler_bei_Einweihung_%22Braunes_Haus%22.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Hitler and Nazi Party treasurer <a href="/wiki/Franz_Xaver_Schwarz" title="Franz Xaver Schwarz">Franz Xaver Schwarz</a> at the dedication of the renovation of the Palais Barlow on <a href="/wiki/Brienner_Stra%C3%9Fe_(Munich)" title="Brienner Straße (Munich)">Brienner Straße</a> in Munich into the <a href="/wiki/Brown_House,_Munich" title="Brown House, Munich">Brown House</a> headquarters, December 1930</div></div></div>
<p>Hitler made a prominent appearance at the trial of two Reichswehr officers, Lieutenants Richard Scheringer and <a href="/wiki/Hanns_Ludin" title="Hanns Ludin">Hanns Ludin</a>, in late 1930.
