Hitler ordered <a href="/wiki/Army_Group_Centre" title="Army Group Centre">Army Group Centre</a> to temporarily halt its advance to Moscow and divert its Panzer groups to aid in the <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Leningrad" title="Siege of Leningrad">encirclement of Leningrad</a> and <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Kiev_(1941)" title="Battle of Kiev (1941)">Kiev</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStolfi1982_286-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStolfi1982-286">[282]</a></sup> His generals disagreed with this change, having advanced within 400 km (250 mi) of Moscow, and his decision caused a crisis among the military leadership.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWilt1981_287-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWilt1981-287">[283]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEvans2008202_288-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEvans2008202-288">[284]</a></sup> The pause provided the Red Army with an opportunity to mobilise fresh reserves; historian Russel Stolfi considers it to be one of the major factors that caused the failure of the Moscow offensive, which was resumed in October 1941 and <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Moscow" title="Battle of Moscow">ended disastrously in December</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStolfi1982_286-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStolfi1982-286">[282]</a></sup> During this crisis, Hitler appointed himself as head of the <span title="German-language text"><i lang="de"><a href="/wiki/Oberkommando_des_Heeres" title="Oberkommando des Heeres">Oberkommando des Heeres</a></i></span>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEvans2008210_289-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEvans2008210-289">[285]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-1987-0703-507,_Berlin,_Reichstagssitzung,_Rede_Adolf_Hitler.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1486" data-file-width="2048" decoding="async" height="160" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-1987-0703-507%2C_Berlin%2C_Reichstagssitzung%2C_Rede_Adolf_Hitler.jpg/220px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-1987-0703-507%2C_Berlin%2C_Reichstagssitzung%2C_Rede_Adolf_Hitler.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-1987-0703-507%2C_Berlin%2C_Reichstagssitzung%2C_Rede_Adolf_Hitler.jpg/330px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-1987-0703-507%2C_Berlin%2C_Reichstagssitzung%2C_Rede_Adolf_Hitler.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-1987-0703-507%2C_Berlin%2C_Reichstagssitzung%2C_Rede_Adolf_Hitler.jpg/440px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-1987-0703-507%2C_Berlin%2C_Reichstagssitzung%2C_Rede_Adolf_Hitler.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-1987-0703-507,_Berlin,_Reichstagssitzung,_Rede_Adolf_Hitler.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Hitler <a href="/wiki/German_declaration_of_war_against_the_United_States" title="German declaration of war against the United States">announcing the declaration of war against the United States</a> to the Reichstag on 11 December 1941</div></div></div>
<p>On 7 December 1941, Japan <a href="/wiki/Attack_on_Pearl_Harbor" title="Attack on Pearl Harbor">attacked the American fleet</a> based at <a href="/wiki/Pearl_Harbor" title="Pearl Harbor">Pearl Harbor</a>, Hawaii. Four days later, Hitler <a href="/wiki/German_declaration_of_war_against_the_United_States" title="German declaration of war against the United States">declared war against the United States</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShirer1960900–901_290-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShirer1960900–901-290">[286]</a></sup> On 18 December 1941, Himmler asked Hitler, "What to do with the Jews of Russia?", to which Hitler replied, <span title="German-language text"><i lang="de">"als Partisanen auszurotten"</i></span> ("exterminate them as partisans").<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBauer20005_291-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBauer20005-291">[287]</a></sup> Israeli historian <a href="/wiki/Yehuda_Bauer" title="Yehuda Bauer">Yehuda Bauer</a> has commented that the remark is probably as close as historians will ever get to a definitive order from Hitler for the genocide carried out during the Holocaust.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBauer20005_291-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBauer20005-291">[287]</a></sup>
</p><p>In late 1942, German forces were defeated in the <a href="/wiki/Second_Battle_of_El_Alamein" title="Second Battle of El Alamein">second battle of El Alamein</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShirer1960921_292-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShirer1960921-292">[288]</a></sup> thwarting Hitler's plans to seize the <a href="/wiki/Suez_Canal" title="Suez Canal">Suez Canal</a> and the Middle East. Overconfident in his own military expertise following the earlier victories in 1940, Hitler became distrustful of his Army High Command and began to interfere in military and tactical planning, with damaging consequences.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKershaw2000b417_293-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKershaw2000b417-293">[289]</a></sup> In December 1942 and January 1943, Hitler's repeated refusal to allow their withdrawal at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Stalingrad" title="Battle of Stalingrad">Battle of Stalingrad</a> led to the almost total destruction of the <a href="/wiki/6th_Army_(Wehrmacht)" title="6th Army (Wehrmacht)">6th Army</a>. Over 200,000 Axis soldiers were killed and 235,000 were taken prisoner.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEvans2008419–420_294-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEvans2008419–420-294">[290]</a></sup> Thereafter came a decisive strategic defeat at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Kursk" title="Battle of Kursk">Battle of Kursk</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShirer19601006_295-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShirer19601006-295">[291]</a></sup> Hitler's military judgement became increasingly erratic, and Germany's military and economic position deteriorated, as did Hitler's health.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBBC_News,_1999_296-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBBC_News,_1999-296">[292]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-1972-025-12,_Zerst%C3%B6rte_Lagerbaracke_nach_dem_20._Juli_1944.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="544" data-file-width="800" decoding="async" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-1972-025-12%2C_Zerst%C3%B6rte_Lagerbaracke_nach_dem_20._Juli_1944.jpg/220px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-1972-025-12%2C_Zerst%C3%B6rte_Lagerbaracke_nach_dem_20._Juli_1944.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-1972-025-12%2C_Zerst%C3%B6rte_Lagerbaracke_nach_dem_20._Juli_1944.jpg/330px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-1972-025-12%2C_Zerst%C3%B6rte_Lagerbaracke_nach_dem_20._Juli_1944.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-1972-025-12%2C_Zerst%C3%B6rte_Lagerbaracke_nach_dem_20._Juli_1944.jpg/440px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-1972-025-12%2C_Zerst%C3%B6rte_Lagerbaracke_nach_dem_20._Juli_1944.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-1972-025-12,_Zerst%C3%B6rte_Lagerbaracke_nach_dem_20._Juli_1944.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The destroyed map room at the <a href="/wiki/Wolf%27s_Lair" title="Wolf's Lair">Wolf's Lair</a>, Hitler's eastern command post, after the <a href="/wiki/20_July_plot" title="20 July plot">20 July plot</a></div></div></div>
<p>Following the <a href="/wiki/Allied_invasion_of_Sicily" title="Allied invasion of Sicily">Allied invasion of Sicily</a> in 1943, <a href="/wiki/Fall_of_the_Fascist_regime_in_Italy" title="Fall of the Fascist regime in Italy">Mussolini was removed from power</a> by King <a href="/wiki/Victor_Emmanuel_III_of_Italy" title="Victor Emmanuel III of Italy">Victor Emmanuel III</a> after a vote of no confidence of the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Council_of_Fascism" title="Grand Council of Fascism">Grand Council of Fascism</a>. Marshal <a href="/wiki/Pietro_Badoglio" title="Pietro Badoglio">Pietro Badoglio</a>, placed in charge of the government, soon <a href="/wiki/Armistice_of_Cassibile" title="Armistice of Cassibile">surrendered to the Allies</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShirer1960996–1000_297-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShirer1960996–1000-297">[293]</a></sup> Throughout 1943 and 1944, the Soviet Union steadily forced Hitler's armies into retreat along the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Front_(World_War_II)" title="Eastern Front (World War II)">Eastern Front</a>. On 6 June 1944, the Western Allied armies landed in northern France in one of the largest <a href="/wiki/Amphibious_warfare" title="Amphibious warfare">amphibious</a> operations in history, <a href="/wiki/Operation_Overlord" title="Operation Overlord">Operation Overlord</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShirer19601036_298-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShirer19601036-298">[294]</a></sup> Many German officers concluded that defeat was inevitable and that continuing under Hitler's leadership would result in the <a href="/wiki/Total_war" title="Total war">complete destruction of the country</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESpeer1971513–514_299-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESpeer1971513–514-299">[295]</a></sup>
</p><p>Between 1939 and 1945, there were many plans to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Assassination_attempts_on_Adolf_Hitler" title="Assassination attempts on Adolf Hitler">assassinate Hitler</a>, some of which proceeded to significant degrees.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKershaw2008544–547,_821–822,_827–828_300-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKershaw2008544–547,_821–822,_827–828-300">[296]</a></sup> The most well known, the <a href="/wiki/20_July_plot" title="20 July plot">20 July plot</a> of 1944, came from within Germany and was at least partly driven by the increasing prospect of a German defeat in the war.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKershaw2008816–818_301-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKershaw2008816–818-301">[297]</a></sup> Part of <a href="/wiki/Operation_Valkyrie" title="Operation Valkyrie">Operation Valkyrie</a>, the plot involved <a href="/wiki/Claus_von_Stauffenberg" title="Claus von Stauffenberg">Claus von Stauffenberg</a> planting a bomb in one of <a href="/wiki/F%C3%BChrer_Headquarters" title="Führer Headquarters">Hitler's headquarters</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Wolf%27s_Lair" title="Wolf's Lair">Wolf's Lair</a> at <a href="/wiki/K%C4%99trzyn" title="Kętrzyn">Rastenburg</a>. Hitler narrowly survived because staff officer <a href="/wiki/Heinz_Brandt" title="Heinz Brandt">Heinz Brandt</a> moved the briefcase containing the bomb behind a leg of the heavy conference table, which deflected much of the blast. Later, Hitler ordered savage reprisals resulting in the execution of more than 4,900 people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShirer19601048–1072_302-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShirer19601048–1072-302">[298]</a></sup>
</p><p>According to British academic <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Dan_Plesch&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Dan Plesch (page does not exist)">Dan Plesch</a>, Hitler was put on the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_War_Crimes_Commission" title="United Nations War Crimes Commission">United Nations War Crimes Commission</a>'s first list of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/War_criminal" title="War criminal">war criminals</a> in December 1944, after determining that Hitler could be held criminally responsible for the acts of the Nazis in occupied countries. By March 1945 at least seven indictments had been filed against him.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPlesch2017158_303-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPlesch2017158-303">[299]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Defeat_and_death">Defeat and death</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hitler_20_April_1945.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="350" data-file-width="299" decoding="async" height="211" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/95/Hitler_20_April_1945.jpg/180px-Hitler_20_April_1945.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/95/Hitler_20_April_1945.jpg/270px-Hitler_20_April_1945.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/9/95/Hitler_20_April_1945.jpg 2x" width="180"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hitler_20_April_1945.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Hitler on 20 April 1945 in his last public appearance, in the Reich Chancellery garden, ten days before he and <a href="/wiki/Eva_Braun" title="Eva Braun">Eva Braun</a> committed suicide</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Stars_%26_Stripes_%26_Hitler_Dead2.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1557" data-file-width="1092" decoding="async" height="257" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Stars_%26_Stripes_%26_Hitler_Dead2.jpg/180px-Stars_%26_Stripes_%26_Hitler_Dead2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Stars_%26_Stripes_%26_Hitler_Dead2.jpg/270px-Stars_%26_Stripes_%26_Hitler_Dead2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Stars_%26_Stripes_%26_Hitler_Dead2.jpg/360px-Stars_%26_Stripes_%26_Hitler_Dead2.jpg 2x" width="180"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Stars_%26_Stripes_%26_Hitler_Dead2.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Front page of the US Armed Forces newspaper, <i><a href="/wiki/Stars_and_Stripes_(newspaper)" title="Stars and Stripes (newspaper)">Stars and Stripes</a></i>, 2 May 1945, announcing Hitler's death</div></div></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Death_of_Adolf_Hitler" title="Death of Adolf Hitler">Death of Adolf Hitler</a></div>
<p>By late 1944, both the <a href="/wiki/Red_Army" title="Red Army">Red Army</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_II" title="Allies of World War II">Western Allies</a> were advancing into Germany. Recognising the strength and determination of the Red Army, Hitler decided to use his remaining mobile reserves against the American and British armies, which he perceived as far weaker.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWeinberg1964_304-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWeinberg1964-304">[300]</a></sup> On 16 December, he launched the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ardennes_Offensive" title="Ardennes Offensive">Ardennes Offensive</a> to incite disunity among the Western Allies and perhaps convince them to join his fight against the Soviets.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECrandell1987_305-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECrandell1987-305">[301]</a></sup> After some temporary successes, the offensive failed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBullock1962778_306-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBullock1962778-306">[302]</a></sup> With much of Germany in ruins in January 1945, Hitler spoke on the radio: "However grave as the crisis may be at this moment, it will, despite everything, be mastered by our unalterable will."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEReesKershaw2012_307-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEReesKershaw2012-307">[303]</a></sup> Acting on his view that Germany's military failures meant it had forfeited its right to survive as a nation, Hitler ordered the destruction of all German industrial infrastructure before it could fall into Allied hands.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBullock1962774–775_308-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBullock1962774–775-308">[304]</a></sup> Minister for Armaments <a href="/wiki/Albert_Speer" title="Albert Speer">Albert Speer</a> was entrusted with executing this <a href="/wiki/Scorched_earth" title="Scorched earth">scorched earth</a> policy, but he secretly disobeyed the order.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBullock1962774–775_308-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBullock1962774–775-308">[304]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESereny1996497–498_309-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESereny1996497–498-309">[305]</a></sup> Hitler's hope to negotiate peace with the United States and Britain was encouraged by the death of US President <a href="/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt" title="Franklin D. Roosevelt">Franklin D. Roosevelt</a> on 12 April 1945, but contrary to his expectations, this caused no rift among the Allies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECrandell1987_305-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECrandell1987-305">[301]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBullock1962753,_763,_780–781_310-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBullock1962753,_763,_780–781-310">[306]</a></sup>
</p><p>On 20 April, his 56th<span class="nowrap"> </span>birthday, Hitler made his last trip from the <span title="German-language text"><i lang="de"><a href="/wiki/F%C3%BChrerbunker" title="Führerbunker">Führerbunker</a></i></span> (Führer's shelter) to the surface. In the ruined garden of the Reich Chancellery, he awarded Iron Crosses to boy soldiers of the <a href="/wiki/Hitler_Youth" title="Hitler Youth">Hitler Youth</a>, who were now fighting the Red Army at the front near Berlin.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBeevor2002251_311-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBeevor2002251-311">[307]</a></sup> By 21 April, <a href="/wiki/Georgy_Zhukov" title="Georgy Zhukov">Georgy Zhukov</a>'s <a href="/wiki/1st_Belorussian_Front" title="1st Belorussian Front">1st Belorussian Front</a> had broken through the defences of General <a href="/wiki/Gotthard_Heinrici" title="Gotthard Heinrici">Gotthard Heinrici</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Army_Group_Vistula" title="Army Group Vistula">Army Group Vistula</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Seelow_Heights" title="Battle of the Seelow Heights">Battle of the Seelow Heights</a> and advanced to the outskirts of Berlin.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBeevor2002255–256_312-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBeevor2002255–256-312">[308]</a></sup> In denial about the dire situation, Hitler placed his hopes on the undermanned and under-equipped <span title="German-language text"><i lang="de">Armeeabteilung Steiner</i></span> (<a href="/wiki/Army_Detachment_Steiner" title="Army Detachment Steiner">Army Detachment Steiner</a>), commanded by <a href="/wiki/Felix_Steiner" title="Felix Steiner">Felix Steiner</a>. Hitler ordered Steiner to attack the northern flank of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Salients,_re-entrants_and_pockets" title="Salients, re-entrants and pockets">salient</a>, while the German <a href="/wiki/9th_Army_(Wehrmacht)" title="9th Army (Wehrmacht)">Ninth Army</a> was ordered to attack northward in a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pincer_attack" title="Pincer attack">pincer attack</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELe_Tissier201045_313-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELe_Tissier201045-313">[309]</a></sup>
</p><p>During a military conference on 22 April, Hitler asked about Steiner's offensive. He was told that the attack had not been launched and that the Soviets had entered Berlin. Hitler asked everyone except Wilhelm Keitel, <a href="/wiki/Alfred_Jodl" title="Alfred Jodl">Alfred Jodl</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hans_Krebs_(Wehrmacht_general)" title="Hans Krebs (Wehrmacht general)">Hans Krebs</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Wilhelm_Burgdorf" title="Wilhelm Burgdorf">Wilhelm Burgdorf</a> to leave the room,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDollinger1995231_314-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDollinger1995231-314">[310]</a></sup> then launched into a tirade against the treachery and incompetence of his commanders, culminating in his declaration—for the first time—that "everything was lost".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJones1989_315-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJones1989-315">[311]</a></sup> He announced that he would stay in Berlin until the end and then shoot himself.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBeevor2002275_316-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBeevor2002275-316">[312]</a></sup>
</p><p>By 23 April the Red Army had surrounded Berlin,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEZiemke196992_317-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEZiemke196992-317">[313]</a></sup> and Goebbels made a proclamation urging its citizens to defend the city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDollinger1995231_314-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDollinger1995231-314">[310]</a></sup> That same day, Göring sent a telegram from <a href="/wiki/Berchtesgaden" title="Berchtesgaden">Berchtesgaden</a>, arguing that since Hitler was isolated in Berlin, Göring should assume leadership of Germany. Göring set a deadline, after which he would consider Hitler incapacitated.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBullock1962787_318-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBullock1962787-318">[314]</a></sup> Hitler responded by having Göring arrested, and in his <a href="/wiki/Last_will_and_testament_of_Adolf_Hitler" title="Last will and testament of Adolf Hitler">last will and testament</a> of 29 April, he removed Göring from all government positions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBullock1962787,_795_319-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBullock1962787,_795-319">[315]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEButlerYoung1989227–228_320-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEButlerYoung1989227–228-320">[316]</a></sup> On 28 April Hitler discovered that Himmler, who had left Berlin on 20 April, was trying to negotiate a surrender to the Western Allies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKershaw2008923–925,_943_321-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKershaw2008923–925,_943-321">[317]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBullock1962791_322-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBullock1962791-322">[318]</a></sup> He ordered Himmler's arrest and had <a href="/wiki/Hermann_Fegelein" title="Hermann Fegelein">Hermann Fegelein</a> (Himmler's SS representative at Hitler's HQ in Berlin) shot.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBullock1962792,_795_323-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBullock1962792,_795-323">[319]</a></sup>
</p><p>After midnight on the night of 28–29 April, Hitler married <a href="/wiki/Eva_Braun" title="Eva Braun">Eva Braun</a> in a small civil ceremony in the <span title="German-language text"><i lang="de">Führerbunker</i></span>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBeevor2002343_324-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBeevor2002343-324">[320]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-will_and_marriage_325-0"><a href="#cite_note-will_and_marriage-325">[e]</a></sup> Later that afternoon, Hitler was informed that <a href="/wiki/Death_of_Benito_Mussolini" title="Death of Benito Mussolini">Mussolini had been executed</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Italian_resistance_movement" title="Italian resistance movement">Italian resistance movement</a> on the previous day; this presumably increased his determination to avoid capture.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBullock1962798_326-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBullock1962798-326">[321]</a></sup>
</p><p>On 30 April 1945, Soviet troops were within a block or two of the Reich Chancellery when Hitler shot himself in the head and Braun bit into a <a href="/wiki/Cyanide" title="Cyanide">cyanide</a> capsule.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELinge2009199_327-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELinge2009199-327">[322]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJoachimsthaler1999160–182_328-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJoachimsthaler1999160–182-328">[323]</a></sup> Their corpses were carried outside to the garden behind the Reich Chancellery, where they were placed in a bomb crater, doused with petrol, and set on fire as the Red Army shelling continued.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELinge2009200_329-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELinge2009200-329">[324]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBullock1962799–800_330-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBullock1962799–800-330">[325]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJoachimsthaler1999217–220,_224–225_331-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJoachimsthaler1999217–220,_224–225-331">[326]</a></sup> Grand Admiral <a href="/wiki/Karl_D%C3%B6nitz" title="Karl Dönitz">Karl Dönitz</a> and Joseph Goebbels assumed Hitler's roles as head of state and chancellor respectively.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKershaw2008949–950_332-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKershaw2008949–950-332">[327]</a></sup>
</p><p>Berlin surrendered on 2 May. The remains of Joseph and <a href="/wiki/Magda_Goebbels" title="Magda Goebbels">Magda Goebbels</a>, the six <a href="/wiki/Goebbels_children" title="Goebbels children">Goebbels children</a>, General <a href="/wiki/Hans_Krebs_(Wehrmacht_general)" title="Hans Krebs (Wehrmacht general)">Hans Krebs</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Blondi" title="Blondi">Hitler's dogs</a> were repeatedly buried and exhumed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVinogradov2005111,_333_333-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVinogradov2005111,_333-333">[328]</a></sup> Hitler and Braun's remains were alleged to have been moved as well, but this is most likely Soviet <a href="/wiki/Disinformation" title="Disinformation">disinformation</a>. There is no evidence that any actual bodily remains of Hitler or Braun—with the exception of the dental bridges—were found by the Soviets, which could be identified as their remains.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJoachimsthaler1999215–225_334-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJoachimsthaler1999215–225-334">[329]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFest2004163–164_335-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFest2004163–164-335">[330]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKershaw2000b1110_336-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKershaw2000b1110-336">[331]</a></sup> While news of Hitler's death spread quickly, a <a href="/wiki/Death_certificate" title="Death certificate">death certificate</a> was not issued until 1956, after a lengthy investigation to collect testimony from 42 witnesses. Hitler's demise was entered as an <a href="/wiki/Presumption_of_death" title="Presumption of death">assumption of death</a> based on this testimony.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJoachimsthaler19998–13_337-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJoachimsthaler19998–13-337">[332]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Holocaust">The Holocaust</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/The_Holocaust" title="The Holocaust">The Holocaust</a> and <a href="/wiki/Final_Solution" title="Final Solution">Final Solution</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r996844942" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p><a href="/wiki/Hitler%27s_prophecy" title="Hitler's prophecy">If the international Jewish financiers in and outside Europe should succeed in plunging the nations once more into a world war, then the result will not be the Bolshevisation of the earth, and thus the victory of Jewry, but the annihilation of the Jewish race in Europe!</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarrus200037_338-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarrus200037-338">[333]</a></sup></p><div class="templatequotecite">— <cite>Adolf Hitler, <a href="/wiki/30_January_1939_Reichstag_speech" title="30 January 1939 Reichstag speech">30 January 1939 Reichstag speech</a></cite></div></blockquote>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Buchenwald_Corpses_60623.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="944" data-file-width="1400" decoding="async" height="148" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Buchenwald_Corpses_60623.jpg/220px-Buchenwald_Corpses_60623.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Buchenwald_Corpses_60623.jpg/330px-Buchenwald_Corpses_60623.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Buchenwald_Corpses_60623.jpg/440px-Buchenwald_Corpses_60623.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Buchenwald_Corpses_60623.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A wagon piled high with corpses outside the crematorium in the liberated <a href="/wiki/Buchenwald_concentration_camp" title="Buchenwald concentration camp">Buchenwald concentration camp</a> (April 1945)</div></div></div>
<p>The Holocaust and Germany's war in the East were based on Hitler's long-standing view that the Jews were the enemy of the German people and that <span title="German-language text"><i lang="de"><a href="/wiki/Lebensraum" title="Lebensraum">Lebensraum</a></i></span> was needed for Germany's expansion. He focused on Eastern Europe for this expansion, aiming to defeat Poland and the Soviet Union and then removing or killing the Jews and <a href="/wiki/Slavs" title="Slavs">Slavs</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGellately1996_339-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGellately1996-339">[334]</a></sup> The <span title="German-language text"><i lang="de"><a href="/wiki/Generalplan_Ost" title="Generalplan Ost">Generalplan Ost</a></i></span> (General Plan East) called for deporting the population of occupied Eastern Europe and the Soviet Union to West Siberia, for use as slave labour or to be murdered;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESnyder2010416_340-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESnyder2010416-340">[335]</a></sup> the conquered territories were to be colonised by German or "Germanised" settlers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESteinberg1995_341-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESteinberg1995-341">[336]</a></sup> The goal was to implement this plan after the conquest of the Soviet Union, but when this failed, Hitler moved the plans forward.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESnyder2010416_340-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESnyder2010416-340">[335]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKershaw2008683_342-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKershaw2008683-342">[337]</a></sup> By January 1942, he had decided that the Jews, Slavs, and other deportees considered undesirable should be killed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShirer1960965_343-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShirer1960965-343">[338]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-recent_scholarship_344-0"><a href="#cite_note-recent_scholarship-344">[f]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Aktion_brand.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3056" data-file-width="2218" decoding="async" height="234" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Aktion_brand.jpg/170px-Aktion_brand.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Aktion_brand.jpg/255px-Aktion_brand.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Aktion_brand.jpg/340px-Aktion_brand.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Aktion_brand.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Hitler's order for <span title="German-language text"><i lang="de"><a href="/wiki/Aktion_T4" title="Aktion T4">Aktion T4</a></i></span>, dated 1 September 1939</div></div></div>
<p>The genocide was organised and executed by <a href="/wiki/Heinrich_Himmler" title="Heinrich Himmler">Heinrich Himmler</a> and <a href="/wiki/Reinhard_Heydrich" title="Reinhard Heydrich">Reinhard Heydrich</a>. The records of the <a href="/wiki/Wannsee_Conference" title="Wannsee Conference">Wannsee Conference</a>, held on 20 January 1942 and led by Heydrich, with fifteen senior Nazi officials participating, provide the clearest evidence of systematic planning for the Holocaust. On 22 February, Hitler was recorded saying, "we shall regain our health only by eliminating the Jews".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENaimark200281_345-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENaimark200281-345">[339]</a></sup> Similarly, at a meeting in July 1941 with leading functionaries of the Eastern territories, Hitler said that the easiest way to quickly pacify the areas would be best achieved by "shooting everyone who even looks odd".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELongerich2005116_346-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELongerich2005116-346">[340]</a></sup> Although no direct order from Hitler authorising the mass killings has surfaced,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMegargee2007146_347-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMegargee2007146-347">[341]</a></sup> his public speeches, orders to his generals, and the diaries of Nazi officials demonstrate that he conceived and authorised the extermination of European Jewry.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELongerich,_Chapter_152003_348-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELongerich,_Chapter_152003-348">[342]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELongerich,_Chapter_172003_349-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELongerich,_Chapter_172003-349">[343]</a></sup> During the war, Hitler repeatedly stated his <a href="/wiki/Hitler%27s_prophecy" title="Hitler's prophecy">prophecy of 1939</a> was being fulfilled, namely, that a world war would bring about the annihilation of the Jewish race.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKershaw2000b459–462_350-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKershaw2000b459–462-350">[344]</a></sup> Hitler approved the <span title="German-language text"><i lang="de"><a href="/wiki/Einsatzgruppen" title="Einsatzgruppen">Einsatzgruppen</a></i></span>—killing squads that followed the German army through Poland, the Baltic, and the Soviet Union<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKershaw2008670–675_351-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKershaw2008670–675-351">[345]</a></sup>—and was well informed about their activities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELongerich,_Chapter_152003_348-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELongerich,_Chapter_152003-348">[342]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMegargee2007144_352-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMegargee2007144-352">[346]</a></sup> By summer 1942, <a href="/wiki/Auschwitz_concentration_camp" title="Auschwitz concentration camp">Auschwitz concentration camp</a> was expanded to accommodate large numbers of deportees for murder or <a href="/wiki/Forced_labour_under_German_rule_during_World_War_II" title="Forced labour under German rule during World War II">enslavement</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKershaw2008687_353-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKershaw2008687-353">[347]</a></sup> Scores of other concentration camps and satellite camps were set up throughout Europe, with several camps devoted exclusively to extermination.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEvans2008map,_p._366_354-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEvans2008map,_p._366-354">[348]</a></sup>
</p><p>Between 1939 and 1945, the <span title="German-language text"><i lang="de"><a href="/wiki/Schutzstaffel" title="Schutzstaffel">Schutzstaffel</a></i></span> (SS), assisted by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Collaboration_with_the_Axis_Powers" title="Collaboration with the Axis Powers">collaborationist</a> governments and recruits from occupied countries, were responsible for the deaths of at least eleven million non-combatants,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERummel1994112_355-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERummel1994112-355">[349]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESnyder2010416_340-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESnyder2010416-340">[335]</a></sup> including the murders of about 6 million Jews (representing two-thirds of the Jewish population of Europe),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHolocaust_Memorial_Museum_356-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHolocaust_Memorial_Museum-356">[350]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-358"><a href="#cite_note-358">[g]</a></sup> and between 200,000 and 1,500,000 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Porajmos" title="Porajmos">Romani people</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHancock2004383–396_359-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHancock2004383–396-359">[352]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHolocaust_Memorial_Museum_356-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHolocaust_Memorial_Museum-356">[350]</a></sup> The victims were killed in concentration and extermination camps, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ghettos_in_Nazi-occupied_Europe" title="Ghettos in Nazi-occupied Europe">ghettos</a>, and through mass executions. Many victims of the Holocaust were murdered in <a href="/wiki/Gas_chamber" title="Gas chamber">gas chambers</a>, while others died of starvation or disease or <a href="/wiki/Extermination_through_labour" title="Extermination through labour">while working as slave labourers</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShirer1960946_360-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShirer1960946-360">[353]</a></sup> In addition to eliminating Jews, the Nazis planned to reduce the population of the conquered territories by 30 million people through starvation in an action called the <a href="/wiki/Hunger_Plan" title="Hunger Plan">Hunger Plan</a>. Food supplies would be diverted to the German army and German civilians. Cities would be razed and the land allowed to return to forest or resettled by German colonists.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESnyder2010162–163,_416_361-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESnyder2010162–163,_416-361">[354]</a></sup> Together, the Hunger Plan and <span title="German-language text"><i lang="de">Generalplan Ost</i></span> would have led to the starvation of 80 million people in the Soviet Union.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDorland20096_362-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDorland20096-362">[355]</a></sup> These partially fulfilled plans resulted in additional deaths, bringing the total number of civilians and prisoners of war who died in the <a href="/wiki/Democide" title="Democide">democide</a> to an estimated 19.3 million people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERummel1994[httpwwwhawaiiedupowerkillsNAZISTAB11GIF_table,_p._112]_363-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERummel1994[httpwwwhawaiiedupowerkillsNAZISTAB11GIF_table,_p._112]-363">[356]</a></sup>
</p><p>Hitler's policies resulted in the killing of nearly two million non-Jewish <a href="/wiki/Nazi_crimes_against_the_Polish_nation" title="Nazi crimes against the Polish nation">Polish civilians</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUS_Holocaust_Memorial_Museum_364-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUS_Holocaust_Memorial_Museum-364">[357]</a></sup> over three million <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/German_mistreatment_of_Soviet_prisoners_of_war" title="German mistreatment of Soviet prisoners of war">Soviet prisoners of war</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESnyder2010184_365-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESnyder2010184-365">[358]</a></sup> communists and other political opponents, <a href="/wiki/Persecution_of_homosexuals_in_Nazi_Germany" title="Persecution of homosexuals in Nazi Germany">homosexuals</a>, the physically and mentally disabled,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENiewykNicosia200045_366-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENiewykNicosia200045-366">[359]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGoldhagen1996290_367-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGoldhagen1996290-367">[360]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Persecution_of_Jehovah%27s_Witnesses_in_Nazi_Germany" title="Persecution of Jehovah's Witnesses in Nazi Germany">Jehovah's Witnesses</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Adventists" title="Adventists">Adventists</a>, and trade unionists. Hitler did not speak publicly about the killings, and seems to never have visited the concentration camps.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDowning200533_368-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDowning200533-368">[361]</a></sup>
</p><p>The Nazis embraced the concept of <a href="/wiki/Racial_hygiene" title="Racial hygiene">racial hygiene</a>. On 15 September 1935, Hitler presented two laws—known as the <a href="/wiki/Nuremberg_Laws" title="Nuremberg Laws">Nuremberg Laws</a>—to the Reichstag. The laws banned sexual relations and marriages between Aryans and Jews and were later extended to include "Gypsies, Negroes or their bastard offspring".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGellately2001216_369-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGellately2001216-369">[362]</a></sup> The laws stripped all non-Aryans of their German citizenship and forbade the employment of non-Jewish women under the age of 45 in Jewish households.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKershaw1999567–568_370-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKershaw1999567–568-370">[363]</a></sup> Hitler's early <a href="/wiki/Nazi_eugenics" title="Nazi eugenics">eugenic</a> policies targeted children with physical and developmental disabilities in a programme dubbed <a href="/wiki/Child_euthanasia_in_Nazi_Germany" title="Child euthanasia in Nazi Germany">Action Brandt</a>, and he later authorised a <a href="/wiki/Euthanasia" title="Euthanasia">euthanasia</a> programme for adults with serious mental and physical disabilities, now referred to as <span title="German-language text"><i lang="de"><a href="/wiki/Aktion_T4" title="Aktion T4">Aktion T4</a></i></span>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEOvery2005252_371-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEOvery2005252-371">[364]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Leadership_style">Leadership style</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-B24543,_Hauptquartier_Heeresgruppe_S%C3%BCd,_Lagebesprechung.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="556" data-file-width="798" decoding="async" height="153" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-B24543%2C_Hauptquartier_Heeresgruppe_S%C3%BCd%2C_Lagebesprechung.jpg/220px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-B24543%2C_Hauptquartier_Heeresgruppe_S%C3%BCd%2C_Lagebesprechung.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-B24543%2C_Hauptquartier_Heeresgruppe_S%C3%BCd%2C_Lagebesprechung.jpg/330px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-B24543%2C_Hauptquartier_Heeresgruppe_S%C3%BCd%2C_Lagebesprechung.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-B24543%2C_Hauptquartier_Heeresgruppe_S%C3%BCd%2C_Lagebesprechung.jpg/440px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-B24543%2C_Hauptquartier_Heeresgruppe_S%C3%BCd%2C_Lagebesprechung.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-B24543,_Hauptquartier_Heeresgruppe_S%C3%BCd,_Lagebesprechung.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Hitler during a meeting at the headquarters of <a href="/wiki/Army_Group_South" title="Army Group South">Army Group South</a> in June 1942</div></div></div>
<p>Hitler ruled the Nazi Party <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Autocratic" title="Autocratic">autocratically</a> by asserting the <span title="German-language text"><i lang="de"><a href="/wiki/F%C3%BChrerprinzip" title="Führerprinzip">Führerprinzip</a></i></span> (leader principle). The principle relied on absolute obedience of all subordinates to their superiors; thus, he viewed the government structure as a pyramid, with himself—the <a href="/wiki/Leaderism" title="Leaderism">infallible leader</a>—at the apex. Rank in the party was not determined by elections—positions were filled through appointment by those of higher rank, who demanded unquestioning obedience to the will of the leader.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKershaw2008170,_172,_181_372-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKershaw2008170,_172,_181-372">[365]</a></sup> Hitler's leadership style was to give contradictory orders to his subordinates and to place them into positions where their duties and responsibilities overlapped with those of others, to have "the stronger one [do] the job".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESpeer1971281_373-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESpeer1971281-373">[366]</a></sup> In this way, Hitler fostered distrust, competition, and infighting among his subordinates to consolidate and maximise his own power. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hitler_Cabinet" title="Hitler Cabinet">His cabinet</a> never met after 1938, and he discouraged his ministers from meeting independently.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEManvellFraenkel200729_374-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEManvellFraenkel200729-374">[367]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKershaw2008323_375-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKershaw2008323-375">[368]</a></sup> Hitler typically did not give written orders; instead, he communicated verbally, or had them conveyed through his close associate <a href="/wiki/Martin_Bormann" title="Martin Bormann">Martin Bormann</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKershaw2008377_376-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKershaw2008377-376">[369]</a></sup> He entrusted Bormann with his paperwork, appointments, and personal finances; Bormann used his position to control the flow of information and access to Hitler.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESpeer1971333_377-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESpeer1971333-377">[370]</a></sup>
</p><p>Hitler dominated his country's war effort during World War II to a greater extent than any other national leader. He strengthened his control of the armed forces in 1938, and subsequently made all major decisions regarding Germany's military strategy. His decision to mount a risky series of offensives against Norway, France, and the Low Countries in 1940 against the advice of the military proved successful, though the diplomatic and military strategies he employed in attempts to force the United Kingdom out of the war ended in failure.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEOvery2005a421–425_378-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEOvery2005a421–425-378">[371]</a></sup> Hitler deepened his involvement in the war effort by appointing himself commander-in-chief of the Army in December 1941; from this point forward, he personally directed the war against the Soviet Union, while his military commanders facing the Western Allies retained a degree of autonomy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKershaw2012169–170_379-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKershaw2012169–170-379">[372]</a></sup> Hitler's leadership became increasingly disconnected from reality as the war turned against Germany, with the military's defensive strategies often hindered by his slow decision-making and frequent directives to hold untenable positions. Nevertheless, he continued to believe that only his leadership could deliver victory.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEOvery2005a421–425_378-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEOvery2005a421–425-378">[371]</a></sup> In the final months of the war, Hitler refused to consider peace negotiations, regarding the destruction of Germany as preferable to surrender.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKershaw2012396–397_380-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKershaw2012396–397-380">[373]</a></sup> The military did not challenge Hitler's dominance of the war effort, and senior officers generally supported and enacted his decisions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKershaw2008171–395_381-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKershaw2008171–395-381">[374]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Family">Family</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Hitler_family" title="Hitler family">Hitler family</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Sexuality_of_Adolf_Hitler" title="Sexuality of Adolf Hitler">Sexuality of Adolf Hitler</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_B_145_Bild-F051673-0059,_Adolf_Hitler_und_Eva_Braun_auf_dem_Berghof.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2812" data-file-width="3640" decoding="async" height="170" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Bundesarchiv_B_145_Bild-F051673-0059%2C_Adolf_Hitler_und_Eva_Braun_auf_dem_Berghof.jpg/220px-Bundesarchiv_B_145_Bild-F051673-0059%2C_Adolf_Hitler_und_Eva_Braun_auf_dem_Berghof.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Bundesarchiv_B_145_Bild-F051673-0059%2C_Adolf_Hitler_und_Eva_Braun_auf_dem_Berghof.jpg/330px-Bundesarchiv_B_145_Bild-F051673-0059%2C_Adolf_Hitler_und_Eva_Braun_auf_dem_Berghof.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Bundesarchiv_B_145_Bild-F051673-0059%2C_Adolf_Hitler_und_Eva_Braun_auf_dem_Berghof.jpg/440px-Bundesarchiv_B_145_Bild-F051673-0059%2C_Adolf_Hitler_und_Eva_Braun_auf_dem_Berghof.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_B_145_Bild-F051673-0059,_Adolf_Hitler_und_Eva_Braun_auf_dem_Berghof.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Hitler in 1942 with his long-time lover <a href="/wiki/Eva_Braun" title="Eva Braun">Eva Braun</a></div></div></div>
<p>Hitler created a public image as a celibate man without a domestic life, dedicated entirely to his political mission and the nation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShirer1960130_150-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShirer1960130-150">[146]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBullock1999563_382-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBullock1999563-382">[375]</a></sup> He met his lover, <a href="/wiki/Eva_Braun" title="Eva Braun">Eva Braun</a>, in 1929,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKershaw2008378_383-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKershaw2008378-383">[376]</a></sup> and married her on 29 April 1945, one day before they both committed suicide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKershaw2008947–948_384-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKershaw2008947–948-384">[377]</a></sup> In September 1931, his half-niece, <a href="/wiki/Geli_Raubal" title="Geli Raubal">Geli Raubal</a>, took her own life with Hitler's gun in his Munich apartment. It was rumoured among contemporaries that Geli was in a romantic relationship with him, and her death was a source of deep, lasting pain.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBullock1962393–394_385-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBullock1962393–394-385">[378]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Paula_Hitler" title="Paula Hitler">Paula Hitler</a>, the younger sister of Hitler and the last living member of his immediate family, died in June 1960.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKershaw20084_19-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKershaw20084-19">[17]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Views_on_religion">Views on religion</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religious_views_of_Adolf_Hitler" title="Religious views of Adolf Hitler">Religious views of Adolf Hitler</a></div>
<p>Hitler was born to a practising Catholic mother and an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anticlerical" title="Anticlerical">anticlerical</a> father; after leaving home, Hitler never again attended <a href="/wiki/Mass_(liturgy)" title="Mass (liturgy)">Mass</a> or received the <a href="/wiki/Sacraments_of_the_Catholic_Church" title="Sacraments of the Catholic Church">sacraments</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKershaw20085_386-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKershaw20085-386">[379]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERißmann200194–96_387-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERißmann200194–96-387">[380]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEToland19929–10_388-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEToland19929–10-388">[381]</a></sup> Speer states that Hitler railed against the church to his political associates, and though he never officially left the church, he had no attachment to it.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESpeer1971141–142_389-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESpeer1971141–142-389">[382]</a></sup> He adds that Hitler felt that in the absence of organised religion, people would turn to mysticism, which he considered regressive.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESpeer1971141–142_389-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESpeer1971141–142-389">[382]</a></sup> According to Speer, Hitler believed that <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Japanese_religions" title="Japanese religions">Japanese religious beliefs</a> or <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a> would have been a more suitable religion for Germans than Christianity, with its "meekness and flabbiness".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESpeer1971143_390-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESpeer1971143-390">[383]</a></sup> Historian <a href="/wiki/John_S._Conway_(historian)" title="John S. Conway (historian)">John S. Conway</a> states that Hitler was fundamentally opposed to the Christian churches.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEConway19683_391-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEConway19683-391">[384]</a></sup> According to Bullock, Hitler did not believe in God, was anticlerical, and held Christian ethics in contempt because they contravened his preferred view of "<a href="/wiki/Survival_of_the_fittest" title="Survival of the fittest">survival of the fittest</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBullock1999385,_389_392-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBullock1999385,_389-392">[385]</a></sup> He favoured aspects of <a href="/wiki/Protestantism" title="Protestantism">Protestantism</a> that suited his own views, and adopted some elements of the Catholic Church's hierarchical organisation, <a href="/wiki/Liturgy" title="Liturgy">liturgy</a>, and phraseology.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERißmann200196_393-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERißmann200196-393">[386]</a></sup> In a 1932 speech, Hitler stated that he was not a Catholic, and declared himself a <a href="/wiki/German_Christians_(movement)" title="German Christians (movement)">German Christian</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWeirGreenberg2022694_394-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWeirGreenberg2022694-394">[387]</a></sup> In a conversation with Albert Speer, Hitler said, "Through me the Evangelical Church could become the established church, as in England."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESpeer1971142_395-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESpeer1971142-395">[388]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hitler_with_Catholic_dignitaries.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="531" data-file-width="800" decoding="async" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Hitler_with_Catholic_dignitaries.jpg/220px-Hitler_with_Catholic_dignitaries.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Hitler_with_Catholic_dignitaries.jpg/330px-Hitler_with_Catholic_dignitaries.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Hitler_with_Catholic_dignitaries.jpg/440px-Hitler_with_Catholic_dignitaries.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hitler_with_Catholic_dignitaries.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Hitler shaking hands with Bishop <a href="/wiki/Ludwig_M%C3%BCller" title="Ludwig Müller">Ludwig Müller</a> in Germany in the 1930s</div></div></div>
<p>Hitler viewed the church as an important politically conservative influence on society,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESpeer1971141_396-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESpeer1971141-396">[389]</a></sup> and he adopted a strategic relationship with it that "suited his immediate political purposes".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEConway19683_391-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEConway19683-391">[384]</a></sup> In public, Hitler often praised Christian heritage and German Christian culture, though professing a belief in an "Aryan Jesus" who fought against the Jews.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESteigmann-Gall200327,_108_397-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESteigmann-Gall200327,_108-397">[390]</a></sup> Any pro-Christian public rhetoric contradicted his private statements, which described Christianity as "absurdity"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHitler200059_398-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHitler200059-398">[391]</a></sup> and nonsense founded on lies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHitler2000342_399-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHitler2000342-399">[392]</a></sup>
</p><p>According to a US <a href="/wiki/Office_of_Strategic_Services" title="Office of Strategic Services">Office of Strategic Services</a> (OSS) report, "The Nazi Master Plan", Hitler planned to destroy the influence of Christian churches within the Reich.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESharkey2002_400-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESharkey2002-400">[393]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBonney20012–3_401-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBonney20012–3-401">[394]</a></sup> His eventual goal was the total elimination of Christianity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPhayer2000_402-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPhayer2000-402">[395]</a></sup> This goal informed Hitler's movement early on, but he saw it as inexpedient to publicly express this extreme position.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBonney20012_403-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBonney20012-403">[396]</a></sup> According to Bullock, Hitler wanted to wait until after the war before executing this plan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBullock1962219,_389_404-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBullock1962219,_389-404">[397]</a></sup>
</p><p>Speer wrote that Hitler had a negative view of Himmler's and <a href="/wiki/Alfred_Rosenberg" title="Alfred Rosenberg">Alfred Rosenberg</a>'s mystical notions and Himmler's attempt to mythologise the SS. Hitler was more pragmatic, and his ambitions centred on more practical concerns.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESpeer1971141,_171,_174_405-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESpeer1971141,_171,_174-405">[398]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBullock1999729_406-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBullock1999729-406">[399]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Health_of_Adolf_Hitler" title="Health of Adolf Hitler">Health of Adolf Hitler</a> and <a href="/wiki/Psychopathography_of_Adolf_Hitler" title="Psychopathography of Adolf Hitler">Psychopathography of Adolf Hitler</a></div>
<p>Researchers have variously suggested that Hitler suffered from <a href="/wiki/Irritable_bowel_syndrome" title="Irritable bowel syndrome">irritable bowel syndrome</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Skin_lesion" title="Skin lesion">skin lesions</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Irregular_heartbeat" title="Irregular heartbeat">irregular heartbeat</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Coronary_sclerosis" title="Coronary sclerosis">coronary sclerosis</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEvans2008508_407-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEvans2008508-407">[400]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Parkinson%27s_disease" title="Parkinson's disease">Parkinson's disease</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBBC_News,_1999_296-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBBC_News,_1999-296">[292]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBullock1962717_408-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBullock1962717-408">[401]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Syphilis" title="Syphilis">syphilis</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBullock1962717_408-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBullock1962717-408">[401]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Giant-cell_arteritis" title="Giant-cell arteritis">giant-cell arteritis</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERedlich1993_409-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERedlich1993-409">[402]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Tinnitus" title="Tinnitus">tinnitus</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERedlich2000129–190_410-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERedlich2000129–190-410">[403]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Monorchism" title="Monorchism">monorchism</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTE''The_Guardian'',_2015_411-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTE''The_Guardian'',_2015-411">[404]</a></sup>
</p><p>In a report prepared for the OSS in 1943, <a href="/wiki/Walter_Charles_Langer" title="Walter Charles Langer">Walter C. Langer</a> of <a href="/wiki/Harvard_University" title="Harvard University">Harvard University</a> described Hitler as a "neurotic <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Psychopath" title="Psychopath">psychopath</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELanger1972126_412-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELanger1972126-412">[405]</a></sup> In his 1977 book <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Psychopathic_God:_Adolf_Hitler" title="The Psychopathic God: Adolf Hitler">The Psychopathic God: Adolf Hitler</a></i>, historian <a href="/wiki/Robert_G._L._Waite" title="Robert G. L. Waite">Robert G. L. Waite</a> proposes that he suffered from <a href="/wiki/Borderline_personality_disorder" title="Borderline personality disorder">borderline personality disorder</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWaite1993356_413-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWaite1993356-413">[406]</a></sup> Historians Henrik Eberle and Hans-Joachim Neumann consider that while he suffered from a number of illnesses including Parkinson's disease, Hitler did not experience pathological delusions and was always fully aware of, and therefore responsible for, his decisions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGunkel2010_414-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGunkel2010-414">[407]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJones1989_315-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJones1989-315">[311]</a></sup>
</p><p>Sometime in the 1930s, <a href="/wiki/Adolf_Hitler_and_vegetarianism" title="Adolf Hitler and vegetarianism">Hitler adopted a mainly vegetarian diet</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBullock1999388_415-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBullock1999388-415">[408]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEToland1992256_416-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEToland1992256-416">[409]</a></sup> avoiding all meat and fish from 1942 onwards. At social events, he sometimes gave graphic accounts of the slaughter of animals in an effort to make his guests shun meat.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWilson1998_417-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWilson1998-417">[410]</a></sup> Bormann had a greenhouse constructed near the <a href="/wiki/Berghof_(residence)" title="Berghof (residence)">Berghof</a> (near <a href="/wiki/Berchtesgaden" title="Berchtesgaden">Berchtesgaden</a>) to ensure a steady supply of fresh fruit and vegetables for Hitler.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcGovern196832–33_418-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcGovern196832–33-418">[411]</a></sup>
</p><p>Hitler stopped drinking alcohol around the time he became vegetarian and thereafter only very occasionally drank beer or wine on social occasions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELinge200938_419-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELinge200938-419">[412]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHitlerTrevor-Roper1988176,_22_January_1942_420-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHitlerTrevor-Roper1988176,_22_January_1942-420">[413]</a></sup> He was a non-smoker for most of his adult life, but smoked heavily in his youth (25 to 40 cigarettes a day); he eventually quit, calling the habit "a waste of money".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEProctor1999219_421-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEProctor1999219-421">[414]</a></sup> He encouraged his close associates to quit by offering a gold watch to anyone able to break the habit.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEToland1992741_422-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEToland1992741-422">[415]</a></sup> Hitler began using <a href="/wiki/Amphetamine" title="Amphetamine">amphetamine</a> occasionally after 1937 and became addicted to it in late 1942.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHestonHeston1980125–142_423-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHestonHeston1980125–142-423">[416]</a></sup> Speer linked this use of amphetamine to Hitler's increasingly erratic behaviour and inflexible decision-making (for example, rarely allowing military retreats).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHestonHeston198011–20_424-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHestonHeston198011–20-424">[417]</a></sup>
</p><p>Prescribed 90 medications during the war years by his personal physician, <a href="/wiki/Theodor_Morell" title="Theodor Morell">Theodor Morell</a>, Hitler took many pills each day for chronic stomach problems and other ailments.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKershaw2008782_425-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKershaw2008782-425">[418]</a></sup> He regularly consumed <a href="/wiki/Amphetamine" title="Amphetamine">amphetamine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Barbiturate" title="Barbiturate">barbiturates</a>, <a href="/wiki/Opiate" title="Opiate">opiates</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Cocaine" title="Cocaine">cocaine</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGhaemi2011190–191_426-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGhaemi2011190–191-426">[419]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPorter2013_427-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPorter2013-427">[420]</a></sup> as well as <a href="/wiki/Potassium_bromide" title="Potassium bromide">potassium bromide</a> and <a href="/wiki/Atropa_belladonna" title="Atropa belladonna">atropa belladonna</a> (the latter in the form of <a href="/wiki/Doktor_Koster%27s_Antigaspills" title="Doktor Koster's Antigaspills">Doktor Koster's Antigaspills</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDoyle20058_428-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDoyle20058-428">[421]</a></sup> He suffered <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ruptured_eardrum" title="Ruptured eardrum">ruptured eardrums</a> as a result of the <a href="/wiki/20_July_plot" title="20 July plot">20 July plot</a> bomb blast in 1944, and 200 wood splinters had to be removed from his legs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELinge2009156_429-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELinge2009156-429">[422]</a></sup> Newsreel footage of Hitler shows tremors in his left hand and a shuffling walk, which began before the war and worsened towards the end of his life.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKershaw2008782_425-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKershaw2008782-425">[418]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ernst-G%C3%BCnther_Schenck" title="Ernst-Günther Schenck">Ernst-Günther Schenck</a> and several other doctors who met Hitler in the last weeks of his life also formed a diagnosis of Parkinson's disease.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEO'Donnell200137_430-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEO'Donnell200137-430">[423]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Legacy">Legacy</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Historiography_of_Adolf_Hitler" title="Historiography of Adolf Hitler">Historiography of Adolf Hitler</a>, <a href="/wiki/Consequences_of_Nazism" title="Consequences of Nazism">Consequences of Nazism</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Neo-Nazism" title="Neo-Nazism">Neo-Nazism</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mahnstein.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="960" data-file-width="1280" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Mahnstein.JPG/220px-Mahnstein.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Mahnstein.JPG/330px-Mahnstein.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Mahnstein.JPG/440px-Mahnstein.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mahnstein.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Outside the building in <a href="/wiki/Braunau_am_Inn" title="Braunau am Inn">Braunau am Inn</a>, Austria, where Hitler was born, is a <a href="/wiki/Hitler_birthplace_memorial_stone" title="Hitler birthplace memorial stone">memorial stone</a> placed as a reminder of the horrors of World War II. The inscription translates as:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEZialcita2019_431-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEZialcita2019-431">[424]</a></sup> <div class="poem">
<p>For peace, freedom<br/>
and democracy<br/>
never again fascism<br/>
millions of dead warn [us]
</p>
</div></div></div></div>
<p>Hitler's suicide was likened by contemporaries to a "spell" being broken.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFest1974753_432-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFest1974753-432">[425]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESpeer1971617_433-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESpeer1971617-433">[426]</a></sup> Public support for Hitler had collapsed by the time of his death and few Germans mourned his passing; Kershaw argues that most civilians and military personnel were too busy adjusting to the collapse of the country or fleeing from the fighting to take any interest.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKershaw2012348–350_434-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKershaw2012348–350-434">[427]</a></sup> According to historian <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/John_Toland_(author)" title="John Toland (author)">John Toland</a>, Nazism "burst like a bubble" without its leader.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEToland1992892_435-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEToland1992892-435">[428]</a></sup>
</p><p>Kershaw describes Hitler as "the embodiment of modern political evil".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKershaw2000bxvii_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKershaw2000bxvii-6">[4]</a></sup> "Never in history has such ruination—physical and moral—been associated with the name of one man", he adds.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKershaw2000b841_436-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKershaw2000b841-436">[429]</a></sup> Hitler's political programme brought about a world war, leaving behind a devastated and impoverished Eastern and Central Europe. Germany suffered wholesale destruction, characterised as <span title="German-language text"><i lang="de"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stunde_Null" title="Stunde Null">Stunde Null</a></i></span> (Zero Hour).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer1995569_437-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer1995569-437">[430]</a></sup> Hitler's policies inflicted human suffering on an unprecedented scale;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDel_TestaLemoineStrickland200383_438-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDel_TestaLemoineStrickland200383-438">[431]</a></sup> according to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/R._J._Rummel" title="R. J. Rummel">R. J. Rummel</a>, the Nazi regime was responsible for the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Democidal" title="Democidal">democidal</a> killing of an estimated 19.3 million civilians and prisoners of war.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERummel1994112_355-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERummel1994112-355">[349]</a></sup> In addition, 28.7<span class="nowrap"> </span>million soldiers and civilians died as a result of military action in the <a href="/wiki/European_theatre_of_World_War_II" title="European theatre of World War II">European theatre of World War II</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERummel1994112_355-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERummel1994112-355">[349]</a></sup> The number of civilians killed during the Second World War was unprecedented in the history of warfare.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMurrayMillett2001554_439-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMurrayMillett2001554-439">[432]</a></sup> Historians, philosophers, and politicians often use the word "<a href="/wiki/Evil" title="Evil">evil</a>" to describe the Nazi regime.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWelch20012_440-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWelch20012-440">[433]</a></sup> Many European countries have <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Laws_against_Holocaust_denial" title="Laws against Holocaust denial">criminalised</a> both the promotion of Nazism and <a href="/wiki/Holocaust_denial" title="Holocaust denial">Holocaust denial</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBazyler20061_441-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBazyler20061-441">[434]</a></sup>
</p><p>Historian <a href="/wiki/Friedrich_Meinecke" title="Friedrich Meinecke">Friedrich Meinecke</a> described Hitler as "one of the great examples of the singular and incalculable power of personality in historical life".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShirer19606_442-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShirer19606-442">[435]</a></sup> English historian <a href="/wiki/Hugh_Trevor-Roper" title="Hugh Trevor-Roper">Hugh Trevor-Roper</a> saw him as "among the 'terrible simplifiers' of history, the most systematic, the most historical, the most philosophical, and yet the coarsest, cruelest, least magnanimous conqueror the world has ever known".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHitlerTrevor-Roper1988xxxv_443-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHitlerTrevor-Roper1988xxxv-443">[436]</a></sup> For the historian <a href="/wiki/John_Roberts_(historian)" title="John Roberts (historian)">John M. Roberts</a>, Hitler's defeat marked the end of a phase of European history dominated by Germany.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERoberts1996501_444-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERoberts1996501-444">[437]</a></sup> In its place emerged the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a>, a global confrontation between the <a href="/wiki/Western_Bloc" title="Western Bloc">Western Bloc</a>, dominated by the United States and other <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a> nations, and the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Bloc" title="Eastern Bloc">Eastern Bloc</a>, dominated by the Soviet Union.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELichtheim1974366_445-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELichtheim1974366-445">[438]</a></sup> Historian <a href="/wiki/Sebastian_Haffner" title="Sebastian Haffner">Sebastian Haffner</a> asserts that without Hitler and the displacement of the Jews, the modern nation state of <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a> would not exist. He contends that without Hitler, the de-colonisation of former European spheres of influence would have been postponed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHaffner1979100–101_446-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHaffner1979100–101-446">[439]</a></sup> Further, Haffner claims that other than <a href="/wiki/Alexander_the_Great" title="Alexander the Great">Alexander the Great</a>, Hitler had a more significant impact than any other comparable historical figure, in that he too caused a wide range of worldwide changes in a relatively short time span.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHaffner1979100_447-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHaffner1979100-447">[440]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="In_propaganda">In propaganda</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Adolf_Hitler_in_popular_culture" title="Adolf Hitler in popular culture">Adolf Hitler in popular culture</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_speeches_given_by_Adolf_Hitler" title="List of speeches given by Adolf Hitler">List of speeches given by Adolf Hitler</a></div>

codecs="vp9, opus"'/><source data-bandwidth="165736" data-framerate="15" data-height="240" data-shorttitle="VP9 240P" data-title="Small VP9 (240P)" data-transcodekey="240p.vp9.webm" data-width="334" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/transcoded/2/27/Adolf_Hitler_at_Berchtesgaden.ogg/Adolf_Hitler_at_Berchtesgaden.ogg.240p.vp9.webm" type='video/webm; codecs="vp9, opus"'/><source data-bandwidth="257096" data-framerate="15" data-height="240" data-shorttitle="WebM 240P" data-title="Small WebM (240P)" data-transcodekey="240p.webm" data-width="334" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/transcoded/2/27/Adolf_Hitler_at_Berchtesgaden.ogg/Adolf_Hitler_at_Berchtesgaden.ogg.240p.webm" type='video/webm; codecs="vp8, vorbis"'/></video> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Adolf_Hitler_at_Berchtesgaden.ogg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Film of Hitler at <a href="/wiki/Berchtesgaden" title="Berchtesgaden">Berchtesgaden</a> (c.<span class="nowrap"> </span>1941)</div></div></div>
<p>Hitler exploited documentary films and newsreels to inspire a <a href="/wiki/Cult_of_personality" title="Cult of personality">cult of personality</a>. He was involved and appeared in a series of propaganda films throughout his political career, many made by <a href="/wiki/Leni_Riefenstahl" title="Leni Riefenstahl">Leni Riefenstahl</a>, regarded as a pioneer of modern filmmaking.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTE''The_Daily_Telegraph'',_2003_448-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTE''The_Daily_Telegraph'',_2003-448">[441]</a></sup> Hitler's propaganda film appearances include:
</p>
<ul><li><span title="German-language text"><i lang="de"><a href="/wiki/The_Victory_of_Faith" title="The Victory of Faith">Der Sieg des Glaubens</a></i></span> (<i>Victory of Faith</i>, 1933)</li>
<li><span title="German-language text"><i lang="de"><a href="/wiki/Triumph_of_the_Will" title="Triumph of the Will">Triumph des Willens</a></i></span> (<i>Triumph of the Will</i>, 1935)</li>
<li><span title="German-language text"><i lang="de"><a href="/wiki/Tag_der_Freiheit:_Unsere_Wehrmacht" title="Tag der Freiheit: Unsere Wehrmacht">Tag der Freiheit: Unsere Wehrmacht</a></i></span> (<i>Day of Freedom: Our Armed Forces</i>, 1935)</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Olympia_(1938_film)" title="Olympia (1938 film)">Olympia</a></i> (1938)</li></ul>
